But `OnReadyButton()` still calls `Network.LaunchGame()` unconditionally whenever `GameConfiguration.IsHotseat()` is true. So the button text is meant to be different in hotseat mode, but it is only advisory UI; if the cached blocker state goes stale or the button remains clickable, the click path itself does not revalidate before launching.
- `g_hotseatNumHumanPlayers` and `g_hotseatNumAIPlayers` are refreshed inside `UpdatePlayerEntry_Hotseat()` rather than at click time. That makes a stale hotseat blocker label/tooltip plausible after slot edits or rebuild timing: the Start banner can lag behind the actual launchable state even though the click path launches immediately.
- Vanilla staging-room launch-blocker hints appear in three distinct places:
  - the centered start banner (`StartLabel`) plus ready control tooltips (`ReadyButton`, `ReadyCheck`, and the local row `ReadyImage`) show the current global blocker or countdown state. For players-connecting and mods-not-ready blockers, the tooltip is expanded with one line per affected player name.
  - each player row's right-side `StatusLabel` shows per-slot readiness or slot-specific problems such as mod download state, invalid-for-map-size, empty human-required slot, unsupported player-count warning, and any `GetPlayerParameterError(playerID)` reason appended in red. Some of those rows also carry a more explicit tooltip (`LOC_INVALID_SLOT_MAP_SIZE_TT`, `LOC_INVALID_SLOT_HUMAN_REQUIRED_TT`, unsupported tooltip text).
  - individual setup selectors can also carry inline invalid markers: the leader/civ pulldown's selected caption and dropdown entries append `value.InvalidReason` in red when a choice is invalid, and generic game-setup parameter controls prepend `parameter.InvalidReason` to the control tooltip.
- Vanilla staging-room parameter-error gating is two-layered: `UpdateReadyButton()` surfaces the first game/player parameter blocker globally by repainting `StartLabel` red and disabling the ready controls, while `UpdatePlayerEntry()` also appends the specific player-parameter error text onto the affected row's `StatusLabel`. This means the player can usually see both the global "cannot start" state and which row/selector caused it.
- Slot removal in vanilla staging is state-based, not structural. The slot pulldown supports `Open`, `AI`, `Closed`, hotseat-only `Human`, and `Swap`; `OnAddPlayer()` only reopens the first closed slot. There is no dedicated "delete/remove slot" action in `StagingRoom.lua`. The only way slots disappear entirely from the room is indirectly through `g_currentMaxPlayers` / map-size changes (`MapConfiguration.GetMaxMajorPlayers()` and related events), which makes higher player IDs non-displayable or invalid for the current map size.
- Vanilla kick-button visibility is narrower than simple slot editability: `UpdatePlayerEntry()` shows Kick only when the local player is the game host, the target slot status is `SS_TAKEN` or `SS_OBSERVER`, the target is not the local player, and the session is not hotseat. Inactive/open/closed/AI rows hide Kick even if other slot controls remain visible.
- Vanilla slot-type pulldowns explicitly disable when they have zero real options (`pullDown.ItemCount < 1`), even before the broader ready/permissions disable pass runs. Any CAI mirror that keeps a placeholder entry for accessibility should still disable the dropdown itself when there are no real slot actions available.
- Staging chat is hidden for Hotseat, Play By Cloud, or when chat is unavailable. Otherwise it has a target pulldown and edit box; committing the box sends chat. `/help` is handled entirely client-side by `ParseInputChatString(...)` returning `printHelp=true`; vanilla then calls `ChatPrintHelp(...)`, which writes localized help directly to the visible chat stack without sending network chat or calling `OnChat(...)`. `ResetChat()` similarly calls `ChatPrintHelpHint(...)` to print the localized command-help hint. Friends/invite controls use `Network.GetFriends()` helpers and are hidden when invites are not allowed. Join code can be shown in the game-summary panel for PBC/Crossplay/EOS Internet and clicking the text copies it to clipboard.
- `EditHotseatPlayer.lua/.xml` is a modal for hotseat player name/password setup. It has name, password, password-verify edit boxes, mismatch status, Accept, and Cancel. Accept only enables when passwords match; it calls `LuaEvents.EditHotseatPlayer_UpdatePlayer(playerID)`.
- `EditHotseatPlayer` mutates live `PlayerConfigurations[playerID]` while the dialog is open: name changes write immediately via `SetHotseatName(...)`, password edits write immediately via `SetHotseatPassword(...)` when the two password boxes match, and a mismatch temporarily clears the stored hotseat password to `""`. Cancel restores the captured initial name/password before closing. Accept does not push a second copy of the values; it only raises `LuaEvents.EditHotseatPlayer_UpdatePlayer(playerID)` so `StagingRoom` refreshes that row.
- `UI/frontEnd/Multiplayer/EditHotseatPlayer.lua` now has a CAI frontend full replacement. The CAI mirror is a modal `MakeGeneralDialog` with three `AlwaysEdit` fields bound to the live vanilla edit boxes through `text_changed` so name/password writes stay immediate, matching vanilla's live `PlayerConfigurations` mutation. The old mismatch status label is intentionally not exposed as a separate CAI widget; when mismatch text is visible, it becomes the Accept button tooltip instead.
- `PlayerChange.lua/.xml` is the in-game hotseat player-handoff popup. It has two modes: a turn-start prompt that sets `TitleText` to the local player's name and optionally requires a hotseat password before Start Turn, and a turn-end `Please Wait` mode driven by `bPlayerChanging` where the dialog box itself is hidden and only `PlayerChangingText` remains visible. `ShowTurnControls()` is the live choke point for that state switch; it clears the password field, toggles `PasswordStack`, enables/disables `OkButton`, and calls `Controls.PasswordEntry:TakeFocus()` when a password is required.
- Vanilla hotseat handoff gives CAI two useful boundaries: `Events.LocalPlayerTurnEnd` for freezing or deferring per-player state, and `Events.LocalPlayerTurnBegin` for restoring the newly active player's state. `PlayerChange` sits between those events visually, but the CAI state swap itself should key off the player-turn events, not the popup lifecycle.
- `PlayerChange.OnOk()` raises `LuaEvents.PlayerChange_Close(Game.GetLocalPlayer())` immediately before the popup is dequeued. That is a good post-accept hook for deferred CAI speech that should wait until the handoff prompt is dismissed.
- `UI/inGame/PlayerChange_CAI.lua` now mirrors `PlayerChange` through a CAI dialog rebuilt from wrapped `ShowTurnControls()`. Prompt mode exposes Start Turn, Save Game, and Menu plus a masked `AlwaysEdit` password field when `PasswordStack` is visible; wait mode exposes the wait text and Menu. The password edit writes through `text_changed` to the live vanilla `Controls.PasswordEntry`, calls vanilla `OnPasswordEntryStringChanged(...)` for enablement parity, uses Enter commit to call vanilla `OnPasswordEntryCommit()`, and disables commit-on-focus-leave so tabbing away does not auto-start the turn. Right before the CAI dialog is pushed, it drops focus from the live `Controls.PasswordEntry` to prevent the native edit box from trapping interaction under the CAI dialog.
- `ConfirmKick.lua` uses `PopupDialog` for host kick confirmation or vote-kick reason selection (AFK, griefing, cheating, cancel). The CAI frontend replacement is a full vanilla-copy override with no CAI widget mirror; its accessibility block installs an extended input-struct handler after `Initialize()` that lets the CAI UI manager handle input first, then directly mirrors the vanilla Escape close path without delegating to the original old-signature `InputHandler`. `ConfirmExit.lua` is a simpler accept/cancel dialog for exit/kick flow. Crossplay login is a message dialog around EOS login state and raises `LuaEvents.EnterCrossPlayLobby()` when login succeeds.
- `PBCNotifyRemind.lua/.xml` is a Play By Cloud notification setup reminder with Options, Accept, and a Do Not Remind checkbox persisted to `Options.SetUserOption("Interface", "PlayByCloudNotifyRemind", ...)`.
- `UI/frontEnd/Multiplayer/PBCNotifyRemind.lua` CAI frontend replacement should mirror it as a simple dialog: title from `Controls.RemindTitle`, body from `Controls.RemindText`, a `Checkbox` bound to the live `DoNotRemindCheckbox` via `IsChecked()` + `DoLeftClick()`, and Options / OK buttons that click the live vanilla buttons. Show/hide is driven by the popup's `ShowHideHandler`, and the extended input handler should let the CAI manager handle Enter/Space/Tab while Escape still closes through `OnAccept()`.
- Civ Royale and Pirates intro popups are multi-page visual tutorials with logo, illustration, description, optional scrollable details, Previous, Next/Play, and Close. On the last page, Play starts matchmaking only if internet lobby service is available. They close automatically when `JoiningRoom` shows.
- Accessibility-shape implication: treat frontend multiplayer as four primary surfaces: MainMenu multiplayer submenu, Lobby browser, HostGame setup, and StagingRoom. Lobby should be a tab/list browser with sortable column reads, join-code dialog, friends list, and live row tooltips. HostGame can mirror the existing setup parameters with a form-like panel and picker dialogs. StagingRoom is the highest-density surface and should likely use a table or tree/list hybrid for player rows plus separate chat, game-summary, friends, and ready/start widgets, preserving all vanilla callbacks (`Network.JoinGame`, `Network.HostGame`, `Network.BroadcastPlayerInfo`, `Network.LaunchGame`, live pulldown callbacks, and modal dialogs).
- `UI/frontEnd/Multiplayer/Lobby.lua` CAI frontend replacement is implemented as a full vanilla-copy override with an accessibility block before `Initialize()`. The CAI panel exposes a games `Tree`, sort dropdown, sort-direction dropdown, refresh button, Join Code, Load, Host/Create, and a persistent friends `List`. PBC lobbies wrap the tree in a `TabControl` whose pages mirror the vanilla shell tabs and switch by clicking the vanilla tab button. Game-row focus selects the vanilla row only when it is not already selected; game-row activate selects and clicks the vanilla Join/Play button when available, so there is no separate CAI Join button. The CAI Join Code button mirrors the live vanilla Join Code button and opens the same `PopupDialog` path that commits through `Network.JoinGameByJoinCode(...)`. Disabled join reasons are included in the row tooltip, but row status such as loading-save/current-turn remains in the label only to avoid repeated speech. Rows expand to player names sourced from the live Members tooltip when available; vanilla does not create visual player rows and the only known source is `serverEntry.Players`, so some lobby types may expose only the player count. Rows also include official/community additional-content groups. Content groups with entries expand to individual mod/game-mode rows and use the group tooltip for owned/required counts; empty groups have no children and use `None` as the tooltip. Vanilla Lua only treats Play By Cloud as a true batch-update source: `IsGameListBatchUpdating()` returns true for PBC only, while Internet and Crossplay both receive trickled `MultiplayerGameListUpdated` entries. CAI therefore tracks its own refresh session from `RebuildGameList()` / `MultiplayerGameListClear` through `MultiplayerGameListComplete`, keeps the tree on a stable `Refreshing game list` placeholder for that whole window, and suppresses incremental rebuilds until the completion event. The focused empty-state row uses different `FocusKey` values for refreshing vs no-results (`empty:refreshing` / `empty:none`) so the tree manager treats `Refreshing game list` and `No games found` as distinct focus states and re-announces when the empty label changes under focus. Live add/remove updates after refresh still rebuild the tree. The persistent friends list mirrors the ChatPanel player-list shape: one always-visible `SubMenu` row per friend, with row speech including the live status and submenu children rebuilt from `BuildFriendActionList(...)`. PBC previous/next page requests are bound to panel-local `Alt+Left` / `Alt+Right` and call the vanilla backend offset refresh path.
- `UI/frontEnd/Multiplayer/StagingRoom.lua` CAI frontend replacement is implemented as a full vanilla-copy override with an accessibility block before `Initialize()`. The CAI panel is pushed from wrapped `OnShow()` only when it is not already on the manager stack, and it is removed only in wrappers around vanilla dequeue chokepoints: `OnHandleExitRequest`, `OnLeaveGameComplete`, `OnBeforeMultiplayerInviteProcessing`, and `OnGameSetupTabClicked`. The root shape is a single panel: player-slot `List`, ready/start action, writable `AlwaysEdit` chat entry that sends via `SendChat` on commit, chat-target `Dropdown`, chat-history `List` of static-text entries, read-only game-summary `EditBox`, Copy Join Code, Play By Cloud End Game and Quit Game, persistent friends `List`, and Game Setup. Player slots are editable `SubMenu` rows when any live slot control is visible/enabled; otherwise they are read-only `MenuItem` rows. Slot labels append ready status plus human/AI/observer/open/closed status, while slot tooltips now compute civ/leader, team, difficulty, and color from live player parameters and game state rather than from often-empty icon-only controls. The slot-type child dropdown uses the selected slot-type explanation as its tooltip, filters out vanilla's swap pseudo-option, and falls back to a disabled `Choose slot type` dummy option when no real slot types are available. Swap is exposed as a separate CAI button that calls vanilla `OnSwapButton(playerID)` under the same non-hotseat/non-PBC/non-matchmaking eligibility used by vanilla. The CAI copy-join-code action mirrors the live join-code text and now falls back to a CAI `Copy the join code to the clipboard.` tooltip when vanilla leaves the join-code text control without one. Real multiplayer chat delivered to the local client is recorded in the CAI chat history and spoken once, non-interrupting, from the wrapped `OnChat` path, including chat sent by the local player; vanilla lobby system chat lines for player connected, disconnected, host migrated, and kicked are also auto-spoken once. CAI also wraps `ChatPrintHelp(...)` so `/help` output is mirrored into CAI chat history as a local-only chat line and auto-spoken with multi-line `SpeakLines(...)`; the chat input tooltip falls back to `LOC_CHAT_HELP_COMMAND_HINT` when the live edit box has no tooltip. The history widget order follows the user's requested flow: chat input, chat target, then history, and the history rows are individual `StaticText` widgets rather than one read-only edit buffer. The leader child dropdown reuses the Advanced Setup `leader, civilization` labels plus leader/civ ability tooltip pattern, and the color child dropdown mirrors vanilla's manual color-option build. Submenu children preserve vanilla mechanics through `OnSlotType`, `OnTeamPull`, player parameter writes, live hotseat edit/kick/add-player callbacks, and `DoLeftClick()` where available. The persistent friends list matches the Lobby/ChatPanel submenu pattern: one always-visible `SubMenu` row per friend, with per-friend action children rebuilt from `BuildFriendActionList(...)` and refreshed on vanilla friend updates plus staging player-state rebuilds that can change invite eligibility.
- Current CAI staging-room hotseat coverage now includes the hotseat edit modal itself: the player-slot submenu still opens `EditHotseatPlayer` through the live vanilla modal path, but the modal is now mirrored by CAI and refreshes off `Realize()` so it stays in sync whether `StagingRoom_SetPlayerID` fires before or after the popup becomes visible.
- Shared UI-manager edit-box note: `EditBoxWidget` now exposes `CommitOnFocusLeave` and defaults it to `true` for writable `AlwaysEdit` parity. StagingRoom chat, `UI/inGame/ChatPanel_CAI.lua`, and the CAI end-game chat in `UI/inGame/EndGameMenu_CAI.lua` all set it to `false` so leaving the input field does not auto-send or auto-commit partially typed chat; Enter remains the explicit send path.
- `UI/inGame/EndGameMenu_CAI.lua` now mirrors the same structural chat pattern as `ChatPanel_CAI.lua` / staging room rather than the older history-editbox + Send-button layout. The CAI end-game chat keeps its own mirrored player-target state, syncs initial state from the live vanilla end-game pulldown label, writes target changes back through `ValidatePlayerTarget(...)`, `UpdatePlayerTargetPulldown(...)`, `UpdatePlayerTargetEditBox(...)`, `UpdatePlayerTargetIcon(...)`, and `PlayerTargetChanged(...)`, and rebuilds its history list from the live vanilla `Controls.ChatStack` on incoming chat, `/help`, and open. This keeps end-game chat behavior native while exposing the newer CAI input -> target -> history navigation order.
- Additional staging-room CAI behavior: for human-target swaps, the separate Swap button now reflects the local pending handshake state as `Swap, on` / `Swap, off`, speaks that state immediately when toggled, and still uses plain `Swap` for instant non-human swaps. Successful swaps are inferred from the local player ID changing across `OnPlayerInfoChanged(...)`; CAI then speaks `Swap successful` and moves focus to the new local slot only if focus was already somewhere inside the CAI player-slot list. Ready-state changes now announce `{player} ready` / `{player} unready`. The CAI ready button keeps the action label as `Ready` / `Unready`, but when a countdown is active its tooltip prepends the live countdown number and, if the button is currently focused, countdown refresh ticks speak the number only. Friend-submenu invite activation now also speaks `Invite sent`.
- Staging-room backend team IDs are zero-based. Player-facing CAI labels keep `TeamTypes.NO_TEAM` unchanged, but format real and newly available teams with `Locale.Lookup("LOC_WORLD_RANKINGS_TEAM", teamID + 1)` so they display as Team 1, Team 2, and so on.

## Sound

- `UI.PlaySound(soundKey)` — plays a UI sound effect
  - `"Main_Menu_Mouse_Over"` — standard hover sound

## Modding

- `Modding.IsModInstalled(modGuid)` — checks if a mod is active
- `Modding.CheckRequirements(mods, saveType)` — validates mod compatibility

## Game State

- `GameConfiguration.GetGameState()` — returns current state
- `GameStateTypes.GAMESTATE_PREGAME` — pre-game state constant

## Network

- `Network.LeaveGame()` — leaves current network session
- `Network.LoadGame(saveData, serverType)` — loads a save file
- `Network.GetFriends()` — returns friends API object

## City Banner XP1 / XP2

- `Civ6Common.lua` exposes `IsExpansion1Active()` and `IsExpansion2Active()`, and CAI can include it directly in in-game UI helpers when behavior needs to branch on Rise and Fall / Gathering Storm.
- Base `CityBannerManager.lua` stores local-city growth and production speech data on top-level controls such as `m_Instance.CityPopulation`, `m_Instance.CityProduction`, `m_Instance.CityPopulationMeter`, and `m_Instance.CityProductionMeter`.
- Expansion 1 and Expansion 2 move those reads into stat-row instance managers instead: `m_StatPopulationIM` allocates a `CityStatPopulation` row whose tooltip lives on `FillMeter`, and `m_StatProductionIM` allocates a `CityStatProduction` row whose tooltip lives on `Button` and whose progress meter lives on `FillMeter`. CAI hotkey reads must support both layouts.
- Expansion 1 and Expansion 2 also move governor info into `m_StatGovernorIM`, with governor detail tooltips on each row `FillMeter`.
- Expansion 1 and Expansion 2 shift city-state quest / trading-post status and city effect icons into instance-manager rows: `m_DetailStatusIM` for status icons such as quests and trading posts, and `m_DetailEffectsIM` for effects such as siege, occupied, housing, amenities, and XP2 power.
- `CityBannerManager` expansion loyalty data can be rebuilt from live `city:GetCulturalIdentity()` calls without the loyalty lens. Useful methods are `GetLoyalty()`, `GetMaxLoyalty()`, `GetLoyaltyPerTurn()`, `GetPotentialTransferPlayer()`, `GetPlayerIdentitiesInCity()`, and `GetIdentitySourcesBreakdown()`.
- Expansion loyalty mini-panel control names are stable enough for CAI tree labels/tooltips: `LoyaltyInfo.LoyaltyPercentageLabel`, `PopulationTop`, `GovernorTop`, `Happiness`, `OtherTop`, `CityStateTop`, `FreeCityTop`, and `IdentityBreakdownStack`.
- GS power banner text can be mirrored from `city:GetPower()` with vanilla loc keys. Firaxis uses `GetFreePower()`, `GetTemporaryPower()`, `GetRequiredPower()`, `IsFullyPowered()`, and `IsFullyPoweredByActiveProject()` together with `LOC_CITY_BANNER_POWERED_CITY`, `LOC_CITY_BANNER_POWERED_CITY_FROM_ACTIVE_PROJECT`, and `LOC_CITY_BANNER_UNPOWERED_CITY`.

# CAI plot-based raw audio

- `CAI_AudioDefinitions.IsPositional` marks raw sounds that must be played through `CAIAudioManager:PlayAtPlot(...)` / `QueueSoundAtPlot(...)`; ordinary `Play(...)` / `QueueSound(...)` reject them so a plot-based handle cannot reuse stale plot parameters. `SCANNER_BEACON` resolves `sounds/UI/scanner_beacon.wav` under the `BEACONS` tag and is the first such definition.
- Plot-based playback deliberately does not use the DLL spatialization system. The audio manager never enables sound spatialization and never sets source/listener position, direction, velocity, or attenuation model. There is no spatial initialization lifecycle. `WorldInput_CAI.lua` includes `hexCoordUtils_CAI` directly for the in-game plot math, while the shared audio manager and load-screen sounds continue initializing normally.
- `CAIHexCoordUtils.displacement(...)` applies nearest-map-wrap folding and odd-row half-column correction. `plotAudioParameters(...)` maps that displacement to ordinary per-handle properties using the Civ V beacon model: pan is `clamp(dcol / 12, -1, 1)`; pitch is one semitone per row capped at one octave through `2 ^ (clamp(drow, -12, 12) / 12)`; volume fades linearly from 1 to 0 over the requested maximum `Map.GetPlotDistance(...)`, defaulting to 30 hexes.
- `PlayAtPlot(soundId, sourcePlotOrId, options)` accepts a Plot or plot id. `options.ListenerPlot` may supply a Plot/id scan origin; otherwise the manager resolves the current CAI cursor live. `options.MaxDistance` overrides the 30-hex default. Active plot sounds recompute ordinary pan, pitch, and volume from live plot ids during the manager update. Queued plot sounds cache ids, not Plot objects, and resolve the default cursor listener at dispatch time.
- Unless `SkipIfPlaying` is explicitly requested, `PlayAtPlot(...)` stops an already-playing handle, applies the new plot's ordinary pan/pitch/volume after that stop, and then calls `PlaySound(...)`. The order matters because stopping may reset per-handle parameters.
- Effective plot volume is the game's live master-volume gain multiplied by the sound's base gain, live tag-setting volume, and current plot-distance gain. `SetSoundVolume(...)` changes the per-sound base gain, so later master, tag, or cursor updates preserve all four components.
- World Scanner item focus plays `SCANNER_BEACON` at the current item's plot, falling back to the current group's plot when needed. Direct item/group cycling, category focus, subcategory focus, search-result injection, and configured auto-focus categories share the same focus helper. Playback captures the current CAI cursor plot as an explicit listener before `ScannerAutoMoveCursor` can snap the cursor to the result, preserving the directional cue instead of immediately recentering it. Silent focus restoration during ordinary rebuild/resort does not replay the beacon.
- `ScannerBeaconEnabled` is a World scanner checkbox setting, enabled by default and sorted before the other scanner settings. `AudioTagVolume_BEACONS` is a 0–100 slider immediately after it and controls the inherited volume of the `BEACONS` audio tag. The shared scanner beacon helper reads the enabled setting live, so disabling it suppresses item-focus beacons, End-key beacon replays, and volume previews without suppressing scanner speech.
- When `AudioTagVolume_BEACONS` changes, World Scanner reapplies audio settings and previews `SCANNER_BEACON` with the source and listener both at the current cursor plot. This produces centered pan, neutral pitch, and full distance gain so the preview demonstrates only the newly selected tag volume.
- `CAIWorldScanner:SpeakCurrentDirection()` is the scanner End-key repeat path. After successfully speaking the current item's direction, it calls the same positional beacon helper so End repeats both the verbal and audio direction. An unavailable/plotless current item retains the existing unavailable speech without playing a beacon.

# CAI navigation wrap audio

- `CAIWidgetHelpers_Navigation.Navigate` can determine a real wrap by comparing the resolved visible-child index with the focused starting index. It emits `navigation_wrap` only after a wrapped focus move succeeds.
- `TabControlWidget:NextPage` / `PreviousPage` emit the same event when Ctrl+Tab page cycling crosses the first/last page boundary. Left/Right tab-strip wrapping uses the generic container path.
- `UIScreenManager:CreateWidget` installs the default event listener and plays raw audio definition `UI_MENU_WRAP` at half the live `UI_NAVIGATION` tag volume; widgets remain responsible only for reporting the navigation event.
- The non-widget world scanner reports category, subcategory, group, and item boundary crossings to the same `UIScreenManager:HandleNavigationWrap(...)` policy method. Initial group or item selection from index `0` is not a wrap.

## World scanner city grouping and apparent distance loss

- The Cities category does not apply a cursor-distance cutoff. It scans every plot revealed to the local observer and validates city centers with `Cities.GetCityInPlot(x, y)`.
- `ScannerGroupCitiesByCivilization` defaults to enabled. Enabled uses `GroupId = "player:" .. ownerID` and the owning-player label; disabled uses `GroupId = "city:" .. ownerID .. ":" .. cityID` and the city label. Groups and their items remain nearest-first relative to the current cursor.
- Cities are classified only by the implicit All subcategory and the relationship subcategories My, City-States, Neutral, and Enemy. Barbarian outposts use a separate subcategory and retain one shared outpost group.

## World scanner zones

- Civ V Access represents a contiguous geography or unexplored region as one scanner instance containing a list of plot indices. Six-neighbor union-find clustering builds the regions, a stable region id is derived independently from the current representative, and the representative is re-resolved to the member nearest the cursor before direction speech or a jump. Unexplored validation also removes cells that have become revealed and drops the instance when none remain.
- Civ VI implements this through `WorldScannerZoneUtils.lua`. Zone items retain their complete `ZonePlotIndices`, a stable component id based on the lowest member plot id, and an optional live member validator. Category construction and `RefreshCategorySort(...)` select the member nearest the captured sort origin; the common current-item boundary reselects from the live navigation cursor and updates the leaf before speech, beacon, auto-move, End, or explicit jump.
- The zone contract survives implicit All duplication, explicit subcategories, custom-category projection, and search cloning because those leaves retain the source item and its member list. Live resolution prunes invalid members and removes an empty zone through the scanner's existing stale-item path.
- `WorldScannerCategoryDefinition.EndExtract` is the post-extraction/finalization hook. Terrain and Geography collect classified plot ids during the shared map pass and partition them afterward; active-lens scanners partition their authoritative `Scan(...)` results directly.
- Geography clusters only revealed plots by six-neighbor adjacency, separately for land and non-lake water. It does not group by Civ VI `GetContinentType()` or reveal the engine's complete continent plot lists: disconnected revealed patches remain separate until the player reveals their connection.
- Unexplored zones match Civ V's grouping and presentation semantics: all unrevealed plots participate regardless of land/water or hidden terrain type, six-neighbor adjacency produces one instance per connected fog component, the minimum member plot id supplies the stable component suffix, and the actionable representative is the surviving member nearest the live cursor. They appear under Terrain/Base with their current hidden-tile count. Before use, live resolution removes newly revealed members, refreshes that count, and prunes an empty instance; a rebuild is authoritative for splits and merges.
- Terrain retains Civ V's independent Fresh Water subcategory. Every revealed plot whose live `plot:IsFreshWater()` result is true appears once under the localized fresh-water group, including mountain or feature plots that also appear in another Terrain subcategory. These remain individual plot instances rather than connectivity zones because they answer the precise “where can I access fresh water?” query.
- The existing Continent active-lens scanner can zone `Map.GetVisibleContinentPlots(continentId)` by continent id plus revealed adjacency. Separate visible patches of the same named continent remain separate instances until exploration connects them, while each instance retains the official continent label.
- The Political / `OwningCiv` lens can zone revealed owned plots by owner id plus adjacency. Adjacent territory of one civilization becomes one instance; disconnected islands, colonies, and enclaves remain separate instances. Existing met-player masking and My/Neutral/Enemy classification remain unchanged.
- The Government lens must not zone only by government type, because adjacent civilizations using the same government would merge and lose their owner/city identity. Use the current semantic identity—government, owner, and purchasing city—as the classification key, then split that set by adjacency. This retains the current government/civilization/city label while collapsing each contiguous city territory into one instance.
- Lens-zone validation should prune members whose revealed state or live classification changed and remove an empty component. Newly revealed territory, ownership transfers, government changes, and component merges/splits remain authoritative on the next active-lens rebuild; nearest-target resolution remains live between rebuilds.
- Power-lens regional coverage uses `city:GetPower():GetPlotsCoveredByRegionalPower()` as its authoritative source. Revealed covered plots are partitioned by city and six-neighbor adjacency, so overlapping ranges from different cities retain their city identity while each connected range becomes one nearest-target zone. Live validation re-resolves the city through `CityManager.GetCity(ownerID, cityID)` and removes plots no longer covered by that city's regional power.
- Gathering Storm exposes official named-place territories through `Territories.GetTerritoryAt(plotIndex)`. `MapLabelManager.lua` groups plots by `territory:GetID()`, reads `territory:GetName()`, and classifies the territory with `GetTerrainClass()`, `IsLake()`, and `IsSea()`. Its named territory layers cover deserts, mountain ranges, lakes, oceans, and seas; `Expansion2_NamedPlaces.xml` supplies `NamedMountains`, `NamedDeserts`, `NamedLakes`, `NamedSeas`, and `NamedOceans` plus civilization-specific name pools.
- Civ V Geography's “ocean” is not a named region: it is each connected component of revealed non-lake water, and lakes are excluded entirely. Gathering Storm water labels instead partition `TERRAIN_CLASS_WATER` territories into lakes, seas, and oceans. A single connected body can therefore contain an ocean territory plus several named sea territories, and `MapLabelManager.lua` may repeat one very large water-territory label at several positions. Official water-territory names cannot safely replace a connected Geography zone's identity one-for-one; either retain connected bodies with generic labels, compose their revealed territory names, or expose named-water territories as a separate scanner view.
- Civ V Terrain separately emits every revealed water plot as its individual base terrain: Coast and Ocean use their ordinary terrain descriptions, while a coast-terrain plot with `plot:IsLake()` is relabeled Lake. Civ VI Terrain follows the same per-plot model. Its special case relabels `TERRAIN_COAST` plus `IsLake()` as Lake, retains non-lake Coast, and lets `TERRAIN_OCEAN` use its official terrain name. This intentional overlap answers a different query from Geography's connected water-body zones.
- Geography retains the connected revealed non-lake-water zone as its actionable identity. Under Gathering Storm, its label is composed from the unique revealed non-lake water territories in that zone: use all official ocean names in localized order when any are present, otherwise use all official sea names, and fall back to localized `Ocean` when no named territory is available. Named seas are intentionally omitted when the same connected zone already exposes an ocean name so global water connectivity does not produce an impractically long label. Outside Gathering Storm, the territory API is never touched and every zone uses the generic label.
- Mountain ranges can therefore use the same scanner-zone target resolver while preferring Gathering Storm's authoritative territory membership and localized `GetName()` value. Defensively partition a territory's revealed mountain plots by adjacency before emitting scanner instances, so a malformed or modded disconnected territory cannot produce a noncontiguous jump zone. In rulesets without the Gathering Storm territory API, fall back to adjacency-clustered revealed mountain plots with a localized generic range label.
- Gathering Storm does not define or display named landmass territories. Its continent label path is separate: `RefreshContinents(...)` gets every plot for a `GameInfo.Continents` id, partitions disconnected regions, and prints the official continent name on sufficiently large regions. Civ VI continents are geological types and can divide one connected landmass; the same continent id can also have disconnected visible patches. A continent label must not be presented as the landmass's authoritative name.
- Prefer descriptive landmass labels over bare ordinals. Build them only from revealed information: mark the component containing the player's capital/start anchor as `Home landmass`; append the revealed Civ VI continent names represented in the component (for example, `Home landmass, Africa and Asia` or `Landmass, Africa`); and use a fixed capital/start-relative direction only when two components would otherwise have the same label. Numbering should be a final collision fallback, not the primary identity. Labels may legitimately gain a continent name or merge when exploration reveals more of the component.

## World scanner category-switch performance

- `CAIWorldScanner:CycleCategory(...)` calls `self:Rebuild()` before finding the next available category. This recreates every category slot and calls `Core.BuildAllCategories(...)`; a category switch therefore rebuilds the complete scanner rather than only the destination category.
- The shared plot pass invokes every eligible plot extractor separately. With the current eight plot-extractor definitions, a fully revealed 6,000-plot map still makes about 48,000 extractor invocations, but extraction is protected once per category rather than wrapping every individual invocation in `pcall`.
- The full rebuild snapshots plot references and reveal state into parallel arrays in one map pass. Every extractor reuses that snapshot, and terrain receives the cached reveal flag for its hidden-plot split. This avoids repeated visibility calls without caching scanner results between rebuilds.
- Category construction still creates separate leaves/groups for implicit `All` and explicit subcategories, but every raw item is now validated once before either view is built.
- Distance and resolved-label sort keys are computed once per validated raw item. Item and group comparators perform pure-Lua key comparisons instead of calling `Map.GetPlotByIndex(...)`, coordinate getters, `Map.GetPlotDistance(...)`, and `Locale.Lookup(...)` at `O(n log n)` comparison frequency.
- Cursor-driven resorting recomputes distance once per unique plot in the current category, updates the duplicated leaves, and then uses the same pure-Lua comparators.
- Each extracted item commonly allocates a table and a closure-backed `Validate` function. Rebuilding all categories discards and recreates those objects, and construction then creates additional leaf, group, and subcategory tables. The resulting allocation and garbage-collection pressure grows with revealed plots and late-game objects.
- Non-plot categories also run during the same rebuild. Unit scanning is shared within one scanner context across My, Neutral, and Enemy categories, but still enumerates every alive player's units and validates the filtered results. Other categories independently query map tacs, waypoints, recommendations, and any currently active dynamic mode or lens.
- Project decision: category switching must continue rebuilding the complete scanner; do not introduce category caching or dirty-category state.
- The full-rebuild optimizations above preserve current category contents, validation, nearest-first ordering, and per-category extraction failure isolation. They do not introduce category caches or dirty state.
# CAI shared dropdown focus restoration

- Dropdown option rows use the widget-owned focus key `<dropdown focus key or id>:option:<index>`, preferring the dropdown's stable `FocusKey` over its runtime `Id`. This distinction matters in `HostGame.lua`, where parameter dropdowns have generated widget IDs on every rebuild but stable `param:<parameter id>` focus keys; using the generated ID makes refresh restoration miss and fall back by path, which can announce a bare numeric option label. Building any focus path to a dropdown descendant silently opens its dropdown ancestor, matching the manager's existing behavior for descendants of collapsed trees and submenus. During `CaptureFocusKey` / `RestoreFocus`, this preserves the open dropdown and option position across passive parent-list refreshes such as staging-room player-state updates and Play By Cloud HostGame parameter refreshes.
- Dropdown commit is distinct from passive refresh: it must write through the selected value before closing so the closed control reads live state, but the setter may synchronously rebuild while focus remains on an option. During `Commit(...)`, `FocusRestoreKeyOverride` makes capture prefer the outer dropdown's stable key while the setter and `value_changed` handlers run. The rebuild therefore restores to the closed replacement dropdown instead of reopening the option row; ordinary passive refresh still restores inside an open dropdown.
## EventPopup behavior and accessibility

- `Assets/UI/Popups/EventPopup.lua` is the base context for data-driven scenario events. There are no DLC Lua replacements for this context in the decompiled game files, so a partial `EventPopup_CAI.lua` replacement can include `EventPopup` directly.
- Requests arrive through either `Events.EventPopupRequest` or `LuaEvents.EventPopupRequest`. Requests for another player are ignored; valid requests are shown at `PopupPriority.Medium`, and later requests are deep-copied into an internal FIFO queue until the current popup closes.
- A popup always exposes its data-row title, optional request/data-row description, request/data-row effects, and optional image caption. One-shot events show Continue plus optional policy, building, unit, and free-form effect unlock icons. Choice events hide Continue and show `ChoiceA` / `ChoiceB`; each choice may have its own unlock icons.
- Each unlock icon's authoritative readable text is the tooltip passed through `AddUnlockIcon(...)`. Type-based unlocks obtain that tooltip from `ToolTipHelper.GetToolTip(typeName, Game.GetLocalPlayer())`; free-form effect unlocks pass their supplied text directly. CAI captures those exact tooltip strings while vanilla populates the current popup instead of reconstructing their displayed descriptions.
- Choice activation sets zero-based `ResponseIndex`, sends `EVENT_POPUP_RESPONSE`, resets the choice controls, and closes. Escape and Return close one-shot events but deliberately do nothing in choice mode. The accessible choice dialog must therefore have no dialog-wide default Enter action; Enter activates a choice only while that choice button has focus.
- `OnClose()` dequeues the current popup and immediately calls `ShowNextQueuedPopup()`. Accessible cleanup must occur before that transition so the next queued event replaces the old CAI dialog without leaving a stale manager-stack entry.
- The decompiled official content contains A/B `EventPopup` definitions only in the Black Death scenario. Its four choice events are `Sick in Body and Soul` when plague is active in at least half the player's cities, `Physician, Heal Thyself` after at least 10 total plague deaths, `Is This God's Judgement?` after at least 30 deaths and again after the scenario counter reaches 15 more deaths, and `The End of the World` after at least 45 total deaths. The first, third, and fourth choices expose free-form effect tooltips; `Physician, Heal Thyself` exposes a Plague Doctor versus Flagellant unit unlock. Australia uses the same popup only for Continue-style exploration and political events, and no other decompiled DLC Lua constructs `ChoiceAText` / `ChoiceBText`.

## Vanilla Gathering Storm World Congress voting flow

- `DLC/Expansion2/UI/Additions/WorldCongressIntro.lua` opens a blocking introduction on `Events.WorldCongressStage1`. The visible action is `Begin Voting`; clicking it dequeues the intro and fires `LuaEvents.WorldCongressIntro_ShowWorldCongress`, which opens `WorldCongressPopup` at stage 1, phase 1.
- A normal-session ballot is a two-phase popup. Phase 1 calls `PopulateResolutions()` and displays each resolution as one card with outcome A and outcome B, each with its own `VotingWidget`, followed by a target pulldown for the currently selected outcome. The voting widget's up control adds a vote and its down control removes one; these are not for/against controls. Clicking the first add-vote control selects A or B and reveals that outcome's target pulldown. Switching outcomes clears the former target and zeroes the other outcome's votes.
- The player must give every resolution at least one vote and select both an outcome and a target. `CanMoveToNextPhase()` keeps `Next` disabled until all three conditions are true for every resolution. The tooltip says `You must vote on all submitted Proposals.`
- Player targets use a leader/civilization pulldown; non-player targets use an alphabetically displayed pulldown of the resolution's possible targets. The stored target remains the game-core index rather than the displayed sort index.
- The first vote on a resolution is free. Additional add/remove controls show the incremental Diplomatic Favor cost/refund; the popup displays remaining Favor at the top and the total resolution cost in the resolution category heading.
- Clicking `Next` moves to phase 2, where `PopulateSummary()` presents the chosen outcomes, targets, and votes for review. `Previous` returns to the editable ballot. `Submit` calls `OnAccept()`, sends one `WORLD_CONGRESS_RESOLUTION_VOTE` operation per voted resolution, then `WORLD_CONGRESS_SUBMIT_TURN`, requests end turn, and disables submission.
- Outside hotseat, submission closes the ballot and opens `WorldCongressBetweenTurns`, which shows every Congress member as waiting/submitted. After resolution processing, `OnWorldCongressResults(...)` reopens `WorldCongressPopup` at stage 4 in results/review mode; its tabs include Last Session Results, Active Effects, and Available Proposals when special-session proposals exist.
- CAI intentionally keeps one pending target per resolution hash rather than per outcome because vanilla populates both outcome pulldowns from the same `PossibleTargets` list and submits only one `PARAM_RESOLUTION_SELECTION`. The CAI target dropdown remains available before outcome/vote selection, its setter changes only pending CAI state, and the CAI Next action writes all valid pending targets into the captured vanilla resolution choices immediately before invoking vanilla Next. Switching A/B therefore preserves the pending target even though vanilla's `OnVoteResolution(...)` clears its own target when the outcome changes.
- The CAI phase-1 Next button cannot mirror `Controls.NextButton:IsDisabled()` while targets are pending outside vanilla. Its live disabled predicate and tooltip validate the CAI outcome and pending target for every normal resolution; it does not add a separate normal-resolution vote blocker because committing an outcome automatically supplies the free first vote. Actionable special-session proposals still validate their required explicit vote. On activation Next commits pending targets, calls vanilla `UpdateNavButtons()`, then clicks the now-valid vanilla Next control.
- World Congress `ResolutionItem` instances all expose the XML root ID `Root`; it is not a unique instance identity. CAI resolution tree rows therefore use the resolution definition hash for `FocusKey` (`res:<hash>`). Using `instanceRoot:GetID()` produces duplicate `res:Root` keys, causing cached tree re-entry to resolve to the first resolution regardless of the previously focused row.
- World Congress stateful widgets follow the shared value-binding contract. Outcome and target dropdowns use `SetValueSetter(...)` for their pending CAI state; silent `SetSelectedIndex(..., true)` is initialization only. Emergency-proposal checkboxes silently seed from `SelectBox:IsSelected()`, bind changes through `SetValueSetter(...)`, and click vanilla only when its live selection differs from the requested value. Do not use `value_changed` as a substitute for a backing setter or retain empty `value_changed` handlers.
- Committing outcome A or B through the CAI resolution dropdown first updates CAI's selected outcome, then clicks that outcome's live vanilla up-vote control when its vote count is zero. Vanilla clears the other outcome while switching, so this commits the resolution's free first vote without duplicating vanilla vote state; recommitting an outcome that already has votes must not add a paid vote. The placeholder option uses vanilla `LOC_WORLD_CONGRESS_TT_NO_VOTING_DOWN`, the same localized first-vote guidance shown on the initial resolution vote button.

## UI-opening input-action eligibility

- CAI's `UI_CAIOpen*` actions delegate to vanilla toggle actions only after checking the same live gate used by their owning HUD context. A failed open must call `Speak(Locale.Lookup(...))`; silently returning leaves a screen-reader user unable to distinguish an unavailable screen from a broken binding.
- `LaunchBar.lua` gates Technology and Civics by capability. Government, Religion, Great People, and Great Works additionally use live launch-button visibility; the Government button is disabled during anarchy and its tooltip contains the remaining-turn reason. Great People, Great Works, and Espionage also honor the vanilla `DISABLE_*_HOTKEY` global parameters.
- Government unlocks after the local culture component reports at least one unlocked policy. Religion unlocks after Faith becomes available. Great Works unlock when an owned city building contains a Great Work; vanilla keeps that screen unlocked after the first discovery. Therefore CAI should use the live LaunchBar control state rather than independently caching displayed or historical values.
- `PartialScreenHooks.lua` unlocks City-States after `Players[local]:GetDiplomacy():HasMet(...)` succeeds for an alive minor, Trade Overview after `GetOutgoingRouteCapacity() > 0`, and Espionage after `GetSpyCapacity() > 0`. Each also has its corresponding game capability gate.
- `UI_CAIOpenCityStates` is handled directly by the `PartialScreenHooks_CAI` `InputActionStarted` wrapper, alongside the other partial-screen actions. After the live contact check, call included `CheckCityStatesUnlocked(localPlayer)` to update vanilla's private cache, then call the actual `OnToggleCityStates()` open function and preserve the click sound.
- The Gathering Storm World Congress ribbon button requires `CAPABILITY_WORLD_CONGRESS` and `Game.GetEras():GetCurrentEra() >= GlobalParameters.WORLD_CONGRESS_INITIAL_ERA`. `GameInfo.Eras[GlobalParameters.WORLD_CONGRESS_INITIAL_ERA].Name` supplies the localized configured era name for failure speech.
- The WorldTracker research/civic chooser hotkeys are blocked while `IsTutorialRunning()` is true and while the corresponding live tracker controls are hidden or disabled. Minimap map search and lens opening are blocked without a local player, during district placement, or in World Builder; lens and map-pin controls add their own capability/visibility/disabled gates. Realtime in-game chat requires the Chat feature and network multiplayer.

## InGame root and accessible quick save/load

- Gathering Storm's `DLC/Expansion2/UI/Replacements/InGame.lua` is the authoritative `InGame` root context. Its header states that mods cannot partially replace this engine-attached context, so CAI imports a full copy as `UI/inGame/InGame.lua` through the `CAIInGame` import action rather than using `ReplaceUIScript`.
- Vanilla handles `PauseMenu` and `QuickSave` through `Events.InputActionTriggered` and `OnInputActionTriggered(actionId)`. CAI removes that exact listener after vanilla initialization and registers one `Events.InputActionStarted` listener which delegates ordinary action ids back to the original function.
- The accessible action is `SaveGame_CAI`, deliberately beginning with `S` so it sorts after vanilla `QuickSave`, which begins with `Q`, when both use `F5`. It checks `CanLocalPlayerSaveGame()` before delegating to `OnInputActionTriggered(Input.GetActionId("QuickSave"))`, and speaks localized success or failure feedback through `Speak()`.
- `LoadGameMenu.lua` owns vanilla `QuickLoad`: its `OnInputActionTriggered(actionId)` checks `CanLocalPlayerLoadGame()`, queries the local quick-save slot with `UI.QuerySaveGameList(...)`, validates required mods in `OnQuickLoadQueryResults(...)`, and delegates the actual load to `Network.LoadGame(...)`. CAI must call this original handler rather than duplicate that asynchronous flow.
- The accessible load action is `ReloadGame_CAI`, deliberately beginning with `R` so it sorts after vanilla `QuickLoad`, which begins with `Q`, when both use `F6`. `LoadGameMenu.lua` replaces its own `InputActionTriggered` listener with an `InputActionStarted` listener. An unavailable load speaks localized failure feedback; an available load pushes a low-priority CAI Yes/No dialog. Yes closes the dialog and calls the original `OnInputActionTriggered(m_QuickloadId)`. The dialog removes itself from the manager stack on `focus_leave`, No, or Escape.

## Cultural victory World Rankings data

- Vanilla `GatherCultureData()` returns alive major players grouped by team. Each player row contains `PlayerID`, `NumStaycationers` from `PlayerCulture:GetStaycationers()`, `NumVisitingUs` from `GetTouristsTo()`, the required foreign-tourist target derived as one more than the largest opposing domestic-tourist count, and `TurnsTillCulturalVictory` when `GetTurnsUntilVictory()` exists.
- Despite the generated Civ VI IDE helper naming its argument `plotID`, `PlayerCulture:GetTouristsFrom(playerID)` takes another player id in World Rankings and returns how many of that civilization's tourists are visiting the owning player. `GetTouristsFromTooltip(playerID)` returns the matching tourism-per-turn, lifetime-tourism, and modifier breakdown. The base World Rankings uses both calls on the local player's culture component for every other alive major player.
- The accessible Culture tree retains team nesting only when a team has multiple alive major players. Teams are sorted by their best member's cultural-victory progress and their live label reports that best progress; players within a team are sorted by individual progress. Singleton players remain top-level rows. Non-local players are leaves whose tooltip contains domestic tourists and a positive turns-to-victory estimate when available. Only the local player's row expands, including when nested under a team, with one flat leaf per other alive major civilization containing its masked leader/civilization identity, tourists visiting the local player, and the authoritative `GetTouristsFromTooltip(...)` breakdown. Unmet identities must remain `LOC_DIPLOPANEL_UNMET_PLAYER` rather than exposing configuration names.
- The expanded vanilla Culture header exposes the main victory explanation plus separate definitions of domestic and visiting tourists. Its three visual column headers also have tooltips explaining domestic tourists, tourists visiting us from that civilization, and total visiting tourists versus the victory target. CAI's advisor leaf joins the main victory explanation with the separate domestic- and visiting-tourist definitions; explicit row labels make the shorter column explanations redundant.
- Gathering Storm cultural-dominance summaries (`we dominate`, `they dominate us`) are produced by `GetCulturalVictoryAdditionalSummary(...)` for the Overall view, not by `ViewCulture()`. Overall also exposes each player's total Tourism-per-turn and Culture-per-turn values. These may be useful Culture-tree enhancements, but they are not missing parity with vanilla's Culture tab. Opening vanilla Culture still activates the `TourismWithUnits` lens; CAI preserves that behavior because its wrapper calls the included `ViewCulture()` before synchronizing the accessible page.
- CAI's Score, Science, Culture, Domination, Religion, Diplomatic, generic/custom, and ordinary Overall victory trees all preserve multi-player team nesting, with singleton players presented directly. Overall uses a victory -> ranked team/singleton -> team-member hierarchy. Its ranking mirrors `PopulateOverallInstance(...)`: team victory progress first, then average primary tiebreak, average secondary tiebreak, highest member generic score, and team id. Each team/singleton row exposes its ordinal place and normalized victory-progress percentage. Known player tooltips contain the localized primary and distinct secondary tiebreak summaries plus `AdditionalSummary`; Culture therefore includes Tourism per turn, Culture per turn, and Gathering Storm cultural dominance. Unmet player rows expose only `LOC_DIPLOPANEL_UNMET_PLAYER`, not hidden tiebreak data. Multiplayer human names and local player/team indicators are stated in text instead of relying on vanilla's visual icon treatments. Scenario-specific Overall branches retain their official narrative/objective presentations rather than forcing the ordinary hierarchy onto incompatible scenario layouts.
- Final ordinary-screen parity implementation (excluding scenarios) retains all substantive vanilla values in Overall, Score, Science, Culture, Domination, Religion, and Diplomatic. The Score advisor prepends `LOC_WORLD_RANKINGS_SCORE_CONDITION` with `Game.GetMaxGameTurns()` before the score explanation. Religion uses vanilla's full `LOC_WORLD_RANKINGS_RELIGION_CONVERT_SUMMARY` wording for both civilizations and teams. Included `ViewCulture()` / `ViewReligion()` calls preserve Tourism and Religion lens activation and reset behavior.
- Science milestone leaves use vanilla `GetTooltipForScienceProject(...)` to expose Spaceport status on the first milestone and prerequisite-technology plus individual-project completion on every applicable milestone. The Gathering Storm advisor includes `LOC_WORLD_RANKINGS_SCIENCE_REQUIREMENT_FINAL` with the configured light-year target. Its light-year progress row is present only after Exoplanet Expedition completion, matching the fifth vanilla meter's gate.
- Science ranking progress mirrors vanilla's per-player progress-data path: for the satellite and Moon Landing stages, a city's project cost enters the denominator only when that city has nonzero progress or the globally completed project supplies full progress; base Mars and Gathering Storm Mars/Exoplanet include each city cost in the denominator. Per-project completion is retained across the city scan so tooltips and the local next-step line identify the first genuinely unfinished project.
- Detailed Score, Science, Culture, Domination, Religion, Diplomatic, and generic/custom rows textually expose vanilla's visual local-player/team state as `You` / `Your team`; known human players also include their multiplayer player name. Reference-only children such as captured-from, converted-civilization, and tourist-source rows retain the ordinary civilization label so the relationship reads naturally.

## Alexander scenario World Rankings replacement

- `DLC/AlexanderScenario/AlexanderScenario.modinfo` registers exactly one `ReplaceUIScript`: Lua context `WorldRankings` is replaced by `UI/Replacements/WorldRankings_AlexanderScenario.lua` when `RULESET_SCENARIO_ALEXANDER` is active. `ARXManager.lua` is imported but is not a UI-context replacement CAI needs to merge.
- The scenario also imports its own `UI/WorldRankings.xml`. That layout replaces the normal Overall contents with live controls `Controls.Alexander1` through `Controls.Alexander8`; the remaining standard ranking containers still exist in the XML.
- `WorldRankings_AlexanderScenario.lua` includes base `WorldRankings`, overrides `ViewOverall()`, and overrides `ShouldCheckCustomVictories()` to return `false`. Its Overall function populates the eight controls with the Alexander quote, scenario rules, the live count of enemy cities, and the live score value `owned cities * 5`.
- CAI's `CAI_WorldRankings` replacement has `LoadOrder 100`, while Alexander's replacement declares no load order, so CAI is the final owner of the shared context. CAI must explicitly compose the scenario behavior; two independent replacements cannot both supply their Lua overrides.
- The correct CAI include chain is ruleset-first: when `GameConfiguration.GetRuleSet()` equals `RULESET_SCENARIO_ALEXANDER`, include `WorldRankings_AlexanderScenario`; otherwise retain the existing XP2 / XP1 / base chain. `GameConfiguration.GetRuleSet()` is available here; do not add a `GameConfiguration.GetValue("RULESET")` fallback. The scenario wrapper already includes base `WorldRankings`, so CAI must not include base a second time.
- CAI's accessible Overall rebuild must also branch for Alexander. The first implementation read `Controls.Alexander1` through `Controls.Alexander8` after the included scenario `ViewOverall()` ran, but in-game testing produced eight present yet blank accessible rows: the imported controls existed while `GetText()` returned empty in CAI's winning replacement context. Do not use those controls as CAI's text source.
- Build three `StaticText` rows from the same authoritative inputs used by `WorldRankings_AlexanderScenario.lua`, joining their components with `[NEWLINE]`. Row one contains scenario display lines 2, 3, and 4 (`LOC_ALEXANDER_SCENARIO_WORLD_RANKING_1`, `_2`, `_3`). Row two contains lines 5 and 6 (`_4`, `_5`). Row three contains lines 7, 8, and 1: live enemy cities (`_6`), live player-zero city score (`_8`), then `LOC_ALEXANDER_ENDGAME_RANKING_LEADER_QUOTE`. For `_6`, count cities owned by alive players whose id is greater than zero; for `_8`, count player-zero cities and multiply by five. Evaluate both counts together from `PlayerManager.GetAlive()` when the third row label is read rather than caching displayed values. Standard tabs that the scenario leaves available can continue using the existing CAI rebuild functions.
- Static integration checks should confirm the ruleset branch precedes expansion selection, the Alexander include is registered by the scenario's `ImportFiles`, all eight scenario localization tags are present once across the three accessible rows in the required order, the third row uses the live city-count helper once for both values, and `ShouldCheckCustomVictories()` remains the included scenario override. In-game testing must open World Rankings in Conquests of Alexander, verify the three grouped Overall rows and current city/score values, verify no duplicate custom-victory tab appears, and smoke-test every remaining tab and close/reopen focus behavior.

## Australia scenario UI replacements

- `DLC/AustraliaScenario/AustraliaScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_AUSTRALIA` and registers three `ReplaceUIScript` actions: `PartialScreenHooks_AustraliaScenario.lua`, `TechTree_AustraliaScenario.lua`, and `WorldRankings_AustraliaScenario.lua`. None declares a load order. CAI's load-order-100 replacements therefore win all three contexts and must explicitly compose the scenario files before adding accessibility behavior.
- The scenario `ImportFiles` action makes all three replacement Lua files available to wildcard `include(...)` calls. It also imports `UI/WorldRankings.xml`, `UI/ARXManager.lua`, and `UI/CivicsTreeIconLoader_AwardSettler.lua`. `WorldRankings.xml` supplies the scenario Overall controls and a shorter score-row layout. `ARXManager.lua` replaces the optional Logitech ARX companion-display implementation through VFS name resolution and does not require CAI integration. The civic icon loader is discovered by the base Civics Tree, Civics Chooser, and World Tracker wildcard include and adds numbered settler-award icons/tooltips.
- `PartialScreenHooks_AustraliaScenario.lua` includes base `PartialScreenHooks` and replaces `CheckSpyCapacity`, `OnDiplomacyMeet`, and `CheckCityStatesUnlocked` with no-ops. This permanently suppresses vanilla espionage and City-States hook unlocking. The scenario database also deletes `CAPABILITY_CITY_STATES_VIEW` and `UNIT_SPY`, but CAI must not rely only on those data consequences: its direct accessible espionage action bypasses vanilla's private unlock flag and should explicitly report the screen unavailable for the Australia ruleset. The CAI include chain should select the Australia wrapper before XP2 / XP1 / base so vanilla hook behavior remains authoritative.
- `TechTree_AustraliaScenario.lua` includes base `TechTree`, caches and overrides `GetEraArtXOffset`, passes `363` as a third argument to the base calculation, then calls `AllocateUI()` / `Resize()`. In the current shipped base file `GetEraArtXOffset(instArt, eraData)` accepts only two arguments, so Lua ignores the scenario's third value and the returned offset is numerically unchanged; the early reallocation also occurs before the normal context `OnInit` rebuild. The wrapper appears to be retained legacy layout code and adds no accessible content, but CAI should still select it before the expansion/base chain to compose the official scenario behavior rather than depend on that implementation accident.
- `WorldRankings_AustraliaScenario.lua` includes base `WorldRankings`, sets `SIZE_SCORE_ITEM_DETAILS` to `69`, replaces `ViewOverall`, and replaces `GatherScoreData`. `GatherScoreData` includes only alive major human players, preventing AI scores from appearing in this economic race. CAI's Score tree already consumes `GatherScoreData()`, so selecting the scenario wrapper automatically preserves this filtering.
- Australia's Overall view contains the localized scenario description; in single-player it lists all eight difficulty thresholds from Settler `200` through Deity `900`, followed by the local player's current difficulty and corresponding required score; and in both single- and multiplayer it contains the Outback title and effects. Multiplayer hides the entire difficulty/threshold block. As with Alexander, CAI should build accessible rows from the authoritative localization tags and live configuration rather than reading scenario layout controls after its winning replacement loads.
- The World Rankings include chain is ruleset-first: Australia, then Alexander, then XP2 / XP1 / base. The accessible Overall rebuild has a dedicated Australia branch. Its first two rows are the scenario description and Outback explanation. The final row derives the live single-player target from `GameInfo.Difficulties`, `PlayerConfigurations[Game.GetLocalPlayer()]:GetHandicapTypeID()`, and the scenario's `{200,300,400,500,600,700,800,900}` thresholds. That current-game row is an expandable `TreeItem`; its eight children run Deity through Settler and each say only `<difficulty name>, <required score>`, avoiding repetition of `Difficulty:` on every row. Multiplayer omits this complete final current-game/threshold tree and retains the two explanation rows. No CAI modinfo entry or copied scenario file is required because the official scenario already imports the wrapper and layout files.
- `CivicsTreeIconLoader_AwardSettler.lua` handles `MODIFIER_PLAYER_GRANT_UNIT_IN_CAPITAL` by `ModifierId`: `CIVIC_AWARD_ONE_SETTLER` uses `LOC_CIVIC_SCENARIO_CROWN_COLONY_DESCRIPTION`, while `CIVIC_AWARD_TWO_SETTLERS` uses `LOC_CIVIC_SCENARIO_GOLD_RUSH_DESCRIPTION`. CAI's shared `GetAwardNames(...)` must recognize those two modifier ids explicitly; the generic modifier cache's single `ModifierValue` is not usable here because later `UnitType`, `Amount`, and `AllowUniqueOverride` arguments overwrite one another.
- The Settler modifiers are civic rewards, not technology rewards. Penal Colony, Crown Colony, Pastoral Leases, Federation, and The Great War each grant one Settler; Gold Rush grants two. Nothing should appear for these rewards in the Technology Tree. Verify them in the Civics Tree or Civics Chooser instead.
- Australia also supplies Continue-style rows to the ordinary data-driven `EventPopup`; it does not replace that UI context. CAI's existing `EventPopup_CAI.lua` integration already covers those events.
- Static verification should confirm all three ruleset-first include branches, explicit accessible espionage suppression, human-only Score data through the included `GatherScoreData`, presence and multiplayer omission of every Overall component, both settler award modifier ids, scenario imports, and `git diff --check`. In-game testing should cover accessible and sighted Tech Tree layout, unavailable City-States and Espionage actions, single-player and multiplayer Overall contents, human-only Score rows, both settler-grant civic descriptions in the chooser/tree/tracker, Australia event popups, remaining World Rankings tabs, and close/reopen focus.

## Black Death scenario UI replacements and composition plan

- `DLC/BlackDeathScenario/BlackDeathScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_BLACKDEATH`. The installed modinfo under the Steam Civ VI DLC directory has the same SHA-256 hash as the decompiled project copy (`B9013A98CD658017C505A124F26458878B24FF5EDD5950DD66B25E288754FE45`), so the decompiled declarations below match the currently installed game.
- The scenario registers eleven `ReplaceUIScript` actions and none declares a load order: `ActionPanel`, `ARXManager`, `UnitPanel`, `CityPanel`, `WorldRankings`, `GovernmentScreen`, `MinimapPanel`, `ModalLensPanel`, `PlotInfo`, `PlotToolTip`, and `TopPanel`. CAI's load-order-100 replacements win nine of these contexts; CAI does not replace `ARXManager` or `ModalLensPanel`. As with Australia and Alexander, every shared context must explicitly compose the scenario before adding accessibility behavior.
- The scenario's `ImportFiles` action exposes the wrappers for `ActionPanel`, `UnitPanel`, `CityPanel`, `WorldRankings`, `GovernmentScreen`, `PlotInfo`, `PlotToolTip`, and `TopPanel`, so those CAI files can use a ruleset-first `include("..._BlackDeathScenario")` branch before their expansion/base selection. `MinimapPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` and `ModalLensPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` are direct replacements but are not in `ImportFiles`. For a non-imported replacement that CAI must compose, follow the established Byzantium/Gaul GovernmentScreen pattern: copy the official wrapper into `UI/Replacements`, add it to the top-level `<Files>` list, register it through a criteria-scoped `<ImportFiles>` action with no load order, then include that VFS copy from the CAI replacement. The official `ModalLensPanel` remains active because CAI does not replace its context and therefore needs no copied import.
- `ActionPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` includes `ActionPanel_Expansion1`, overrides `OnRefresh()`, delegates to `BASE_OnRefresh()`, and then hides the era/age score, threshold, countdown, animation, and tooltip controls. A CAI ruleset-first include preserves the sighted scenario panel. The accessible `ActionPanelSpeakEraAge` action should honor the same suppression instead of exposing a UI feature the scenario deliberately removes.
- `UnitPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` includes base `UnitPanel`, adds five `EXECUTE_SCRIPT` actions through `GetUnitActionsTable()`—Study, Minister, Pacify, Purge, and Holy Fervor—and adds the scenario's remaining-charge property to the visual stats list. CAI's action menu already consumes the returned vanilla action table and invokes each stored callback, so including the wrapper should expose all five commands without reimplementing them. CAI's Charges summary reads ordinary `ReadUnitData` charge fields, not the scenario property used by `FilterUnitStatsFromUnitData`; it needs a Black Death property fallback so the remaining scenario charges are spoken too. The wrapper also adds only presentation animations for the five activation reasons.
- `CityPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` includes base `CityPanel` and makes `PurchaseTileCheck` available only to England. CAI's combined city-management action already reads that control's live visibility, so including the wrapper preserves the civilization gate.
- `PlotInfo_BlackDeathScenario.lua` turns England's purchase-plot mode into Coerce. It lists only plague-bearing plots, charges 10 Gold, applies `CoerceTurns = 10` plus the current start turn, shows remaining coerced turns for an already affected plot, and refreshes when plot properties change. CAI must include this wrapper so activation delegates to the scenario's `OnClickPurchasePlot`. The shared city-management helper currently derives purchase candidates and costs from `CityManager.GetCommandTargets()` and `city:GetGold():GetPlotPurchaseCost()`, which does not describe Coerce; its Black Death branch must instead mirror the scenario's plague/coercion properties and live 10-Gold affordability before announcing or enabling a plot.
- `PlotToolTip_BlackDeathScenario.lua` includes `PlotTooltip_Expansion2`, adds `CoerceTurns` to fetched plot data, and appends the localized remaining-turn label for an England-owned coerced plot. A ruleset-first include supplies that field to `PlotToolTip_CAI.lua`; CAI must still expose it through a dedicated `coerceTurns` information helper because the accessible helper pipeline does not consume vanilla's `GetDetails()` list. The helper mirrors the official visibility, local ownership, and England checks and uses `LOC_PLOTINFO_COERCED_TURNS_LABEL`. It appears immediately after `fallout` in the default plot information, automatic cursor-move keys, and `PlotReadStats` bucket.
- `WorldRankings_BlackDeathScenario.lua` includes base `WorldRankings` and adds `g_victoryData.VICTORY_BLACKDEATH_SCENARIO`. Its progress text reports completed civics and technologies against the scenario endpoints (`CIVIC_MIDDLE_CLASS` and `TECH_INVENTION`), and its score is the greater of the two completion fractions. It also replaces the sighted Overall-instance population code. Once the wrapper is selected before Australia, Alexander, and expansion/base files, CAI's existing custom-victory discovery and generic victory views can consume the added `g_victoryData` entry; a separate hard-coded Overall branch should not be necessary unless in-game testing shows scenario-specific presentation missing.
- `GovernmentScreen_BlackDeathScenario.lua` is a 2,734-line full replacement based on the base screen, paired with the scenario's imported `GovernmentScreen.xml`; it is not an Expansion 2 extension. CAI must select it before Dramatic Ages / expansion variants so Lua and XML remain compatible. France's trait adds a third wildcard slot; scenario code treats that third wildcard/core slot index 2 as the Papal slot, displays its localized name and description, charges 4 Faith per turn while filled, and deliberately permits incomplete governments. CAI's generic policy-slot widgets must identify that live slot for France and append the Papal name/upkeep description to both empty and filled slot speech. Confirmation should continue mirroring the live vanilla `ConfirmPolicies` state, which preserves the scenario's empty-slot allowance. The wrapper's standalone `OnFaithChanged()` is never registered anywhere in the shipped DLC and contains an undefined `kPlayer`; the gameplay script, not this dead UI function, performs the per-turn Faith deduction and clears/notifies when upkeep cannot be paid.
- `TopPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` includes `TopPanel_Expansion2`, subtracts the filled Papal slot's 4-Faith upkeep from France's displayed per-turn Faith, and appends the localized upkeep line to the Faith tooltip. Selecting the wrapper preserves the sighted yields and makes its `GetFaithTooltip()` available to CAI, but CAI's direct Faith speech and yield-tree value currently call `GetFaithYield()` themselves and must apply the same live subtraction. This wrapper also includes `BlackDeathScenario_PopupHandler`; losing the wrapper loses scenario event-response plumbing, not just TopPanel presentation.
- `BlackDeathScenario_PopupHandler.lua` maps user-defined notification activation to `LuaEvents.EventPopupRequest`, then maps `Events.EventPopupResponse` to a networked `PlayerOperations.EXECUTE_SCRIPT` request whose `OnStart` is `EventPopupChoice`. CAI's notification center already activates the vanilla rail handler, which raises the expected user-notification Lua event, and `EventPopup_CAI.lua` already delegates choice/Continue clicks to vanilla. Loading the official handler through the TopPanel composition is therefore the missing link; CAI should not duplicate this network flow.
- `MinimapPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` creates the Plague lens toggle, maintains the `PlagueHighlight` overlay from each plot's `Plague` property on a 0–10 grayscale, handles the scenario `LensPlague` action (default Insert), and raises `LuaEvents.OnPlagueLensOn`. `ModalLensPanel_BlackDeathScenario.lua` listens for that event and displays the localized plague legend. CAI imports and includes a copy of the official Minimap wrapper, with one small getter exposing its scenario-created button to the accessible lens list. The accessible Plague entry activates the official `LuaEvents.OnViewPlagueLens` path. CAI's `InputActionStarted` wrapper removes the included `OnInputActionTriggered` listener only after late initialization and delegates ordinary actions to the included handler, allowing Insert to reach the official scenario implementation.
- `CityBannerManager_BlackDeathScenario.lua` and `CityBannerManager.xml` are imported rather than registered as a replacement. Expansion city banners wildcard-include `CityBannerManager_*`, so the official plague-indicator instance and method extensions compose automatically with `CityBannerManager_CAI.lua`. CAI reads the visible `banner.m_StatPlagueIM` tooltip through its dedicated `blackDeathIndicator` information key. That key belongs only to the city Identity and status bucket, whose `CityBannerReadIdentityStatus` action is bound to number 1; it is not folded into the generic status collector or repeated in another bucket.
- `EndGameMenu_BlackDeathScenario.lua` is also imported and is loaded by base `include("EndGameMenu_", true)`. It adds the Black Death victory ribbon, background, movie, sound, and color style automatically; CAI does not need to copy or register it. The scenario's ARX manager is confined to the optional Logitech companion display and requires no CAI integration.
- Use ruleset-first includes for the eight wrappers already imported by the scenario. For a wrapper omitted from the scenario's `ImportFiles`, copy and import it through CAI as described above instead of manually reproducing its behavior. Retain the official direct `ModalLensPanel`, and add accessibility-specific live-data handling only for Coerce, Papal-slot speech/upkeep, scenario charges, the Plague lens entry, and city-banner plague status.
- A safe implementation order is: (1) compose TopPanel and event plumbing; (2) compose UnitPanel, CityPanel, PlotInfo, and PlotToolTip plus the Coerce/charge speech gaps; (3) compose GovernmentScreen and Papal slot/upkeep speech; (4) import/include the non-imported Minimap wrapper and expose its Plague lens; (5) compose ActionPanel and WorldRankings; (6) verify wildcard CityBanner and EndGame behavior. In-game testing should cover all four playable civilizations, all five scenario unit commands including disabled reasons and charge changes, England Coerce targeting/cost/duration, France's third wildcard slot and 4-Faith upkeep/automatic clearing, plague tooltip/banner/lens behavior and Insert remapping, all four A/B plague events through notification activation and response, Black Death victory progress/end-game presentation, hidden era controls/action, every remaining World Rankings tab, and close/reopen focus behavior.
- CAI implementation 2026-07-17 follows that composition plan. The eight scenario-imported shared contexts select their Black Death wrappers before expansion/base files. The copied Minimap wrapper is registered in CAI's top-level file list and in a `BlackDeathScenario`-scoped import action with no load order, then selected first by `MinimapPanel_CAI.lua`. Its official Plague toggle, overlay, `LensPlague`, and `OnViewPlagueLens` behavior remain authoritative; CAI adds only the button getter and accessible list entry. The `InputActionTriggered` listener is removed only after the included late initializer registers it, and ordinary `InputActionStarted` actions delegate to the included scenario handler.
- The Plague lens is a custom overlay, not one of the engine lens layers consumed by the ordinary `Events.LensLayerOn/Off` scanner path. `MinimapPanel_CAI.lua` therefore publishes authoritative `ExposedMembers.CAIPlagueLensActive` state plus `LuaEvents.CAIPlagueLensChanged` from the included scenario's on/off and refresh functions, and the World Scanner rebuilds its Active lens category from that event. Black Death implements plague effects through Civ VI's Fallout manager; the official PlotToolTip already announces `LOC_TOOLTIP_PLOT_CONTAMINATED_TEXT` as localized `PLAGUE-STRICKEN: N turns`. Do not add a second active-lens plot helper. The scanner reads the same `Game.GetFalloutManager():GetFalloutTurnsRemaining(plotIndex)` source and official localization, enumerates only revealed positive-duration plots, groups them from highest to lowest, and validates the live duration before focusing an item.
- Black Death city-management state is scenario-specific.
