England's active purchase layer enumerates `Map.GetCityPlots():GetPurchasedPlots(city)`, retains only plots whose live `Plague` property is positive, reads `Coerce` with `RefreshObjectState` when available, uses the scenario's 10-Gold cost, and exposes coerced plots separately from affordable and too-expensive targets. Accessible activation still calls the included scenario `OnClickPurchasePlot`; success immediately announces the localized 10-turn coerced state while the networked property operation completes.
- The accessible Government policy tree recognizes France's core slot index `RULES.PapalSlotIndex - 1`, prepends the localized Papal slot name, and exposes its upkeep description whether empty or filled. TopPanel uses one shared live Faith-yield helper for direct speech and the yield tree, subtracting `RULES.PapalSlotUpkeep` only while France's Papal slot is filled. Unit charge speech reads the scenario's `Charges` / `MaxCharges` properties, and the number 1 city-banner Identity and status bucket reads the visible `m_StatPlagueIM` indicator tooltip.
- The scenario GovernmentScreen is based on an older base revision and does not define the later global extension points `GetPolicyFromCatalog()` or `IsReadOnly()`. Accessibility code must not call either unconditionally. Its policy fallback should reproduce the official catalog record from `GameInfo.Policies[policyType]` plus `GameInfo.Types[policyType].Hash`, localizing `Name` and `Description`; its read-only fallback is false because the scenario has no World Congress policy-lock state. The scenario does retain `IsAbleToChangePolicies()`, `IsPolicyTypeActive()`, `IsPolicyTypeLegalInRow()`, `SetActivePolicyAtSlotIndex()`, and `RemoveActivePolicyAtSlotIndex()`.

## Nubia scenario UI replacements and composition plan

- `DLC/NubiaScenario/NubiaScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_NUBIA` and registers exactly one formal `ReplaceUIScript`: Lua context `WorldRankings` is replaced by `UI/Replacements/WorldRankings_NubiaScenario.lua`. The replacement declares no load order, so CAI's load-order-100 `WorldRankings_CAI.lua` wins and must explicitly compose the scenario wrapper. The installed modinfo and all four relevant UI files have the same SHA-256 hashes as the decompiled copies; the installed modinfo hash is `80215E115BD7147BF96DB4B36DE7084453D08F0F59F7DA60F8F0B16A993763F2`.
- The scenario also imports `TechFilterFunctions_NubiaScenario.lua`, `EndGameMenu_NubiaScenario.lua`, `ARXManager.lua`, the World Rankings wrapper, and `WorldRankings.xml`. The XML remains the active layout through the scenario import and requires no CAI copy. ARXManager targets only the optional Logitech companion display and does not need accessibility composition.
- `WorldRankings_NubiaScenario.lua` includes base `WorldRankings`, hides Overall through `ShouldShowOverall()`, forces Score to remain available through `ForceShowScore()`, and replaces the custom-victory data/view path. `GatherGenericData()` counts each alive major player's `BUILDING_TEMPLE_AMUN` buildings into `PlayerScore` and sums them into `TeamScore`; the custom `ViewGeneric()` sorts by team score and displays progress as `<count>/7`. The scenario victory requirement confirms that seven Temples to Amun is the target.
- Nubia's World Rankings deliberately suppress singleton players whose id is greater than 1 in both Score and custom-victory views. Player ids 0 and 1 are Egypt and Nubia; ids 2 through 7 are the six scheduled invasion civilizations. CAI must preserve that filter instead of exposing invasion-player rows that the official scenario hides. Team rows with more than one member retain the official behavior.
- The correct CAI include chain is ruleset-first: when `GameConfiguration.GetRuleSet()` is `RULESET_SCENARIO_NUBIA`, include `WorldRankings_NubiaScenario`; otherwise continue through the other scenario, expansion, and base branches. The wrapper already includes base World Rankings, so it must not be followed by a second base include. No modinfo entry or copied scenario file is needed because the scenario already imports the wrapper.
- Including the wrapper is necessary but not sufficient for accessible parity. CAI's generic victory row currently announces the player and requirements but not `playerData.PlayerScore`. For `VICTORY_NUBIA_SCENARIO`, the accessible rebuild must sort by live `TeamScore`, retain the official main-player filter, and announce the live Temple count against the target of seven. The accessible Score rebuild must apply the same official singleton-player filter. The forced Score tab should retain the scenario's localized `LOC_WORLD_RANKINGS_SCORE_DETAILS`, which explains that score determines victory level but cannot itself win the scenario.
- `TechFilterFunctions_NubiaScenario.lua` is loaded automatically by the base `TechFilterFunctions.lua` wildcard include used by both Tech Tree and Civics Tree. It adds `CIVIC_BOARDGAMES_ATHLETICS` to the Units filter because that civic grants a Great General. CAI should not copy or manually reproduce it; verify that the accessible Civics Tree Units filter includes Boardgames and Athletics after the World Rankings composition change.
- `EndGameMenu_NubiaScenario.lua` is loaded automatically by base `include("EndGameMenu_", true)` and adds the style for `VICTORY_NUBIA_SCENARIO`. CAI's EndGameMenu replacement extends the original context after that wildcard path and needs no Nubia-specific include or copy. Verify the Nubia victory ribbon, background, movie, sound, color, final score/ranking, and accessible end-game controls.
- Nubia sends its introduction, mercenary, invasion, high-priestess, and named-general messages through the ordinary data-driven `EVENT_POPUP_REQUEST` flow. It does not replace EventPopup. CAI's existing `EventPopup_CAI.lua` should expose their localized title, description, effects, image caption, and Continue control without scenario-specific code. Nubia also deletes `UNITOPERATION_PLANT_FOREST`; the existing UnitPanel guard for scenario-pruned operation rows covers the known load hazard.
- A safe implementation order is: (1) add the Nubia ruleset-first World Rankings include; (2) add the Temple-count/sort and main-player filtering to the accessible custom-victory view; (3) apply the official main-player filter to accessible Score; (4) statically verify the wildcard TechFilter and EndGameMenu paths plus EventPopup and UnitPanel coverage. In-game testing should cover no Overall tab, the default Temple-victory tab, live Egypt/Nubia Temple totals from 0 through 7, ordering changes as temples are built, absence of the six invasion players, the forced Score explanation and final-score rows, Boardgames and Athletics under the Civics Units filter, several scenario event popups, conquest and Temple victories, end-game presentation/controls, remaining available tabs, and close/reopen focus.
- CAI uses generic custom-victory presentation capture instead of adding a ruleset branch to `RebuildGenericTree` for every scenario. After the selected official wrapper is included, CAI wraps its global `PopulateGenericInstance` and `PopulateGenericTeamInstance` functions. While the official `ViewGeneric(victoryType)` renders, it captures the exact ordered player/team records actually populated, their stable ids, the scenario-returned data tables, and the nonempty visible text/tooltips written to their instance controls. The CAI tree is built from that normalized capture immediately after the original view returns. This preserves wrapper-owned filtering, ordering, labels, scores, and requirements; Nubia's `PlayerID < 2` condition and `Score` text therefore flow through without a Nubia-only accessible rebuild.
- Keep `Game.GetVictoryRequirements(...)`, `GameEffects` requirement text/state, `GameInfo.Victories` description, and player/team name helpers as the semantic fallback when a populated instance exposes no useful presentation text. Add conventional structured fallbacks for `PlayerScore` / `TeamScore`, but do not announce arbitrary data-table field names because Civ VI provides no labels or schema for scenario-defined fields. Preserve `FocusKey` from team/player ids rather than captured display text.
- The capture cannot guarantee compatibility with every third-party victory. Civ VI defines no structured custom-victory UI contract beyond overridable Lua functions: a mod may replace `ViewGeneric` completely, use local population functions, or paint unrelated custom controls directly. `ExposedMembers.CAIWorldRankings.RegisterGenericVictoryAdapter(victoryType, adapter)` covers those exceptions. `adapter.GetRows(victoryType, capturedRows)` returns replacement normalized rows or nil to use the structured fallback; adapter failures and invalid return values are logged and fall back to the captured rows. Official wrappers that use the vanilla global population hooks require no adapter; custom Overall replacements remain a separate presentation problem.
- Capture runs only during the active original `ViewGeneric` call, clears the model before each render, and rebuilds the accessible tree afterward with focus capture/restore. It retains captured strings and the immediately returned data records, not vanilla instance controls that InstanceManager may recycle. Refresh reruns the authoritative official view/capture path before changed progress is announced.
- The same authoritative capture is applied to `PopulateScoreInstance` and `PopulateScoreTeamInstance`. Accessible Score rows therefore inherit scenario-owned filtering and order while retaining CAI's expandable score-category children. This automatically preserves Nubia's exclusion of singleton invasion players and Australia's human-only Score data.
- CAI implementation 2026-07-17 selects `WorldRankings_NubiaScenario` before expansion/base files. The custom-victory capture exposes the wrapper's live `<Temple count>/7` text and Egypt/Nubia filtering; the Score capture preserves its equivalent official filtering. No Nubia file copy, modinfo registration, or new localization is required.
- `HAS_7_TEMPLES` has no `VictoryProgress` requirement-text mapping, so `GameEffects.GetRequirementTextKey(requirementID, "VictoryProgress")` legitimately returns nil. Never pass that nil into `GameEffects.GetRequirementText`, whose second argument must be a string. Skip the structured requirement child when the key is absent and retain the captured official `<Temple count>/7` row plus victory description as the accessible presentation.

## Indonesia/Khmer scenario UI replacements and composition plan

- `DLC/Indonesia_KhmerScenario/Indonesia_KhmerScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_INDONESIA_KHMER` and registers four formal `ReplaceUIScript` actions: `CityStates`, `TradeOverview`, `ReligionScreen`, and `WorldRankings`. None declares a load order, so CAI's load-order-100 replacements win and must explicitly compose all four official wrappers. The installed and decompiled modinfo files have the same SHA-256 hash, `7EB60F5CCDBCCD15FF778B68814A14D2EBB8D15747B7705EC54F466DC05C7B38`.
- The same scenario action imports all four wrappers, `WorldRankings.xml`, `CivilopediaPage_Resource.lua`, `EndGameMenu_Indonesia_KhmerScenario.lua`, and `ARXManager.lua`. It also lists `UI/GreatWorksOverview.lua`, but that file is absent from both the installed Windows DLC and the decompiled copy; this is a stale manifest entry, not scenario behavior that CAI must reproduce. ARXManager targets only the optional Logitech companion display.
- The correct include rule for each formal replacement is ruleset-first. `CityStates_CAI.lua`, `TradeOverview_CAI.lua`, `ReligionScreen_CAI.lua`, and `WorldRankings_CAI.lua` should include their corresponding `*_Indonesia_KhmerScenario` wrapper when the active ruleset matches, then skip the ordinary expansion/base branch because each official wrapper already includes its base file. No scenario file copy and no CAI modinfo registration are needed because the DLC already imports every wrapper and its World Rankings XML.
- `CityStates_Indonesia_KhmerScenario.lua` adds the scenario's `MARITIME` city-state type. It supplies the Maritime icon atlas, localized type name and tooltip, recognizes leaders inheriting from `LEADER_MINOR_CIV_MARITIME`, and returns the scenario-specific 1/3/6-envoy bonuses. CAI's accessible city-state tree already calls the overridable `GetCityStateType`, `GetTypeName`, and `GetBonusText` functions, so selecting this wrapper should make the Maritime type and all three bonuses accessible without a parallel ruleset branch. The sighted panel also retains its official Maritime icon.
- `TradeOverview_Indonesia_KhmerScenario.lua` overrides `GetCityStateIcon()` so routes to scenario Maritime city-states use `ICON_CITYSTATE_MARITIME`. This is a sighted icon-only change; CAI's accessible route names and yield details do not depend on the icon. The shipped function refers to an undefined `leader` variable in its direct-leader comparison, but all playable Maritime city-state leaders inherit from `LEADER_MINOR_CIV_MARITIME`, so its `leaderInfo.InheritFrom` path covers the scenario data. Preserve the official wrapper rather than duplicating this function.
- `ReligionScreen_Indonesia_KhmerScenario.lua` makes `AddLockedBeliefs()` a no-op because every scenario religion is founded by the gameplay script with a preset pantheon plus three preset religion beliefs. The pantheon is stored and displayed separately; `religion.Beliefs` therefore legitimately contains three items. Selecting the wrapper preserves the sighted screen's lack of locked slots, but CAI's independent `BuildBeliefsSection()` currently hardcodes a maximum of four and adds a false fourth `Locked belief slot` with the ordinary Apostle evangelization tooltip. Under `RULESET_SCENARIO_INDONESIA_KHMER`, the accessible belief count must use three as its total and must not synthesize locked rows. The already-founded scenario religion should expose no setup or evangelization flow.
- Civ VI exposes no database or gameplay API for a religion's maximum belief-slot count. Base `ReligionScreen.lua` declares `NUM_MAX_BELIEFS = 4` as a private local and uses it only inside the overridable global `AddLockedBeliefs(religion)`. Do not duplicate that constant in CAI or add per-ruleset slot totals. After the active official/mod wrapper populates a selected religion, treat the live children of `Controls.ViewReligionBeliefs` as authoritative: `AddUnlockedBeliefs()` creates the unlocked instances and the active `AddLockedBeliefs()` implementation creates or suppresses locked instances. Build the accessible count and locked rows from that live presentation while continuing to derive unlocked belief names/descriptions from `religion.Beliefs`. This automatically gives four total slots in vanilla and three in Path to Nirvana, and also follows compatible mods that preserve the standard Religion Screen stack/population contract. No solution can guarantee parity with every arbitrary mod: a full replacement may use unrelated custom controls or local-only population functions. When the standard stack is unavailable, the safe fallback is to expose the known unlocked beliefs without inventing locked slots; a bespoke adapter is required for a custom presentation that wants more.
- `WorldRankings_Indonesia_KhmerScenario.lua` overrides `ViewOverall()` and fills ten custom `IndonesiaKhmer1` through `IndonesiaKhmer10` controls from the imported scenario XML. The rows are static scenario rules: unavailable systems, promoted/trainable religious units, unique city-state suzerain behavior, 300 religious pressure from envoys, traders not creating roads, and the three scoring sources. The last three scoring explanations use the official example values: 1 point per follower, 20 points per foreign converted city, and 1 point per Faith per turn.
- World Rankings therefore needs two layers of composition. Include the official wrapper first so its layout and sighted Overall behavior survive. Then add a `RULESET_SCENARIO_INDONESIA_KHMER` branch to CAI's `RebuildOverallTree()` that exposes the same ten localized rows in the wrapper's exact displayed order (`1, 2, 3, 4, 10, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9`) and uses the same formatting arguments (`1,1`, `20,20`, and `1,1`). The standard score view remains authoritative: the gameplay script updates `ScoringScenario1` from followers, `ScoringScenario2` from foreign cities following the religion, and `ScoringScenario3` from live Faith yield; the scenario scoring database maps them to the visible Score categories with multipliers 1, 20, and 1. CAI's existing official Score population capture and expandable category rows should consume these values without an Indonesia/Khmer-specific score implementation.
- `CivilopediaPage_Resource.lua` is a same-name wildcard replacement loaded by base `include("CivilopediaPage_", true)`, which still runs through `CivilopediaScreen_CAI.lua`. It changes the Cloves and Cinnamon suzerain source from Zanzibar to scenario Palembang and omits ordinary resource placement rows. This should compose automatically; do not copy or directly include it from CAI.
- `EndGameMenu_Indonesia_KhmerScenario.lua` is loaded automatically by base `include("EndGameMenu_", true)` alongside `EndGameMenu_CAI.lua`. It styles the scenario's Score victory as a Religious victory. Scenario data supplies five historic rankings at 0/250/500/750/1000 points and disables One More Turn. CAI's generic end-game results/ranking controls should consume that live base presentation without a scenario branch.
- A safe implementation order is: (1) add the ruleset-first includes to CityStates, TradeOverview, ReligionScreen, and WorldRankings; (2) add the ten-row accessible World Rankings Overall branch; (3) suppress CAI's ordinary fourth locked-belief row and use a three-belief total for this ruleset; (4) statically verify that Score capture still exposes only the three scenario categories and that Civilopedia/EndGame wildcard files remain loaded; (5) test the scenario in game. The test matrix should cover all four Maritime city-states and their 1/3/6-envoy bonuses, a trade route involving a Maritime city-state, all seven preset religions with a separate pantheon plus three religion beliefs and no locked/setup controls, the two grouped Overall rules rows in official line order, live follower/foreign-city/Faith score categories and totals, Palembang as the Cloves/Cinnamon suzerain source, Score-victory religious styling, all five historic ranking thresholds, disabled One More Turn, remaining available tabs, and close/reopen focus.
- CAI implementation 2026-07-17 selects the four official Indonesia/Khmer wrappers before ordinary expansion/base files. CityStates' accessible tree consumes the wrapper's live Maritime type and envoy-bonus functions, while TradeOverview and ReligionScreen preserve their official sighted behavior. World Rankings exposes the ten localized scenario-rule lines in the wrapper's exact order as two accessible rows joined with `[NEWLINE]`: displayed lines 1-6 are the rules row and displayed lines 7-10 are the scoring row. The standard captured Score presentation remains authoritative for live scenario categories. Civilopedia and EndGame continue composing through their existing wildcard hosts; no scenario file copy, modinfo entry, or new localization is required.
- CAI's religion belief presentation now reads the visible children of `Controls.ViewReligionBeliefs` whenever the requested religion is the live selected sighted view. Recycled InstanceManager children are excluded through `IsHidden()`, and the count is never allowed below the structured unlocked count. Both the section summary and synthesized locked rows use that live total. If the requested religion is not currently selected, the standard stack is unavailable, or the sighted religion view is hidden, CAI falls back to the unlocked `religion.Beliefs` count and creates no speculative locked rows. This yields 3 of 3 with no locked row in Path to Nirvana and retains vanilla's ordinary 3 of 4 plus locked row when the official screen creates it.

## Poland scenario UI replacements and composition plan

- `DLC/PolandScenario/PolandScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_POLAND`. Its only formal `ReplaceUIScript` replaces the `WorldRankings` context with `UI/Replacements/WorldRankings_PolandScenario.lua` and declares no load order. CAI's load-order-100 `WorldRankings_CAI.lua` therefore wins and must explicitly include the official wrapper for this ruleset. The scenario also imports `ReligionScreen.lua`, `UnitFlagManager.lua`, the World Rankings wrapper and XML, and `ARXManager.lua`.
- `WorldRankings_PolandScenario.lua` includes base `WorldRankings`, changes only the Overall view, and preserves the ordinary Score view. Its imported XML supplies `ViennaInfo1` and `ViennaInfo2`. The first control contains, in order, Vienna history paragraph 1, Vienna history paragraph 2, and Ottoman Janissary history paragraph 1, separated by double newlines; the second contains Ottoman Janissary history paragraph 2. The last paragraph states the scenario's essential Vienna-survival objective.
- Add `RULESET_SCENARIO_POLAND` to the ruleset-first include chain in `WorldRankings_CAI.lua`, before expansion/base selection. Add a Poland branch to `RebuildOverallTree()` with one stable `StaticText` row containing all four official paragraphs in order, joined with `[NEWLINE]`. Use the four existing localization tags and `JoinLines`; no new player-facing localization is needed. The existing authoritative Score capture should remain unchanged.
- `ReligionScreen.lua` is an imported same-name full replacement, so CAI's existing `include("ReligionScreen")` should resolve it automatically when the Poland scenario action is active. The official file suppresses player religion founding and belief-addition flows, creates Catholicism or Orthodoxy from gameplay script data, exposes both religions, and hardcodes the scenario maximum to two founded religions because `GREAT_PERSON_CLASS_PROPHET` is deleted. It still renders four belief instances: two preset beliefs plus two locked rows.
- CAI must not infer setup availability independently in this scenario. `ReligionScreen_CAI.lua:GetSetupState()` should return nil for `RULESET_SCENARIO_POLAND`, preserving the official read-only scenario behavior even if engine belief counters look pending. The accessible `All Religions` summary must report a maximum of two for this ruleset; the generic `Map_GreatPersonClasses` lookup returns zero because the scenario deletes the Prophet class. Continue using the live visible belief-instance count for belief totals and locked rows, so the official two-of-four presentation remains authoritative.
- `UnitFlagManager.lua` is also an imported same-name full replacement. `UnitFlagManager_CAI.lua` already calls `include("UnitFlagManager")` for ordinary rulesets, so the official scenario manager should compose automatically and retain its invasion-unit colors. The official wrapper exports `GetTribeName(index)`, mapping scenario tribe indices 0 through 9 to the localized Teutonic Knights, Rus, Horde, Moldavian, Ottoman, and Swedish faction names used by the sighted flag tooltip.
- Add an accessible Poland invasion-faction detail to CAI unit-flag information. Resolve it from the included official `GetTribeName(unit:GetBarbarianTribeIndex())` rather than duplicating the index table. Include the nonempty result in default and requested unit-flag details with a stable semantic key. This is separate from Barbarian Clans mode: Poland does not enable that mode, so the current `barbarianClan` helper never exposes these names.
- The scenario's early-warning and invasion-arrival messages use ordinary `EVENT_POPUP_REQUEST` records (`SCENARIO_POLAND_EARLY_WARNING` and `SCENARIO_POLAND_INVASION_HERE`) with their complete localized message in `EventEffect`. `EventPopup_CAI.lua` should expose them without Poland-specific code. Verify the warning's invader, turns, and target city and the arrival's invader name, plus repeated/queued warnings.
- Scenario Setup is data-driven: three playable nobles, fixed 60 turns, fixed Duel map, Score-only victory, and leader/civilization abilities and unique items. The existing accessible Scenario Setup should consume these records without a new screen replacement. LoadScreen should consume `LOC_LOADING_INFO_POLAND_SCENARIO` through its existing live presentation.
- Vienna falling triggers `DEFEAT_VIENNA`; reaching the fixed turn limit uses ordinary Score victory. The scenario supplies thirteen historic end-game thresholds from 0 through 1000. No EndGame UI file is imported, so CAI's generic end-game controls should expose the defeat, winner/score, and historic ranking without a scenario branch. World Rankings Score should expose the three playable nobles and live category details through the existing score capture.
- Scenario Great People, writings, portraits, buildings, units, beliefs, Civilopedia queries, and city-state data are database additions or removals with no dedicated UI wrapper beyond the files above. Existing Great People, Great Works, Production, Civilopedia, city-state, religion, unit, and city accessibility paths should consume the live data. Treat these as regression coverage rather than new scenario branches unless an in-game mismatch is found.
- Safe implementation order: (1) compose the Poland World Rankings wrapper and add its merged Overall row; (2) make Religion Screen setup read-only and correct the two-religion maximum; (3) expose official invasion-faction names from UnitFlagManager; (4) run static include/order/localization and modinfo checks; (5) execute the scenario test matrix.
- In-game matrix: Scenario Setup with all three nobles and fixed settings; LoadScreen narration; World Rankings Overall row order and Score details; Catholic and Orthodox religion views, two-of-four belief presentation, no setup/add-belief controls, and `2/2` founded religions; Teutonic, Rus, Horde, Moldavian, Ottoman, and Swedish unit faction names through cursor/unit-flag reads; early-warning, arrival, and queued event popups; new scenario units/buildings/Great People/Great Works/Civilopedia pages; Vienna survival through turn 60 and Vienna-loss defeat; all thirteen end-game ranking thresholds; multiplayer/hotseat player filtering if supported; close/reopen and focus restoration; ordinary base-game World Rankings, Religion Screen, unit flags, and Barbarian Clans regressions.
- CAI implementation 2026-07-17 selects `WorldRankings_PolandScenario` before other scenario/expansion/base files and exposes all four official Vienna/Janissary paragraphs as one stable Overall row joined with `[NEWLINE]`. Religion setup is always read-only under `RULESET_SCENARIO_POLAND`, and the founded-religion summary uses the official maximum of two while belief totals still follow the live scenario Religion Screen. UnitFlagManager adds a `polandInvasion` information helper and default key; both ordinary and detailed unit reads call the included official `GetTribeName()` for visible barbarian invasion units. No scenario files, modinfo registrations, or new localization tags are required.

## Vikings scenario UI replacements and composition plan

- `DLC/VikingsScenario/VikingsScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_VIKINGS`. The installed and decompiled manifests have the same SHA-256 hash, `6B5F05148CD513726456690EA9FAC96A027E3158987A75E393C3A618B73FDE06`. It registers two formal replacements with no load order: `PartialScreenHooks_VikingsScenario.lua` and `WorldRankings_VikingsScenario.lua`. CAI's load-order-100 replacements therefore win both contexts and must explicitly compose the official wrappers. The scenario also imports its same-name full `ReligionScreen.lua` and its custom `WorldRankings.xml`.
- Add a ruleset-first branch to `PartialScreenHooks_CAI.lua` that includes `PartialScreenHooks_VikingsScenario` before the expansion/base chain. The wrapper deliberately keeps Espionage and City States locked by overriding `CheckSpyCapacity`, `OnDiplomacyMeet`, and `CheckCityStatesUnlocked`. Scenario data also deletes `CAPABILITY_CITY_STATES_VIEW`, `CAPABILITY_TOP_PANEL_ENVOYS`, and the Government Screen diplomacy filter. CAI's City States action should continue reporting the capability-based unavailable message, while its Espionage action needs an explicit Vikings suppression equivalent to Australia's because the Vikings data does not delete an Espionage capability.
- Add `WorldRankings_VikingsScenario` to the ruleset-first include chain in `WorldRankings_CAI.lua`. Its imported layout has three Overall controls. Accessible Overall should expose three stable rows matching those controls: `LOC_VIKING_SCENARIO_DESCRIPTION`; `LOC_VIKING_SCENARIO_RELIGION_DESCRIPTION`; and the three scoring explanations joined in official order with the wrapper's exact numeric arguments: `(25, 10, 50, 25, 10)`, `(1000, 500, 300, 100)`, and `(50, 50, 1, 10, 1, 5)`. The ordinary Score view remains authoritative and should continue through CAI's captured score population.
- Vikings scoring retains City, Population, Great Person, Trade, and Pillage line items with scenario multipliers, plus `ScoringScenario1` for Vinland Admiral discovery awards, `ScoringScenario2` for religion-dependent raiding/settling awards, and `ScoringScenario3` for the final-turn Viking Gold/Faith bonus. The existing Score tree reads the live category totals and should require no scenario branch. The gameplay script announces individual awards only through `Game.AddWorldViewText`, which has no existing CAI capture path; persistent totals remain available on demand in World Rankings. Treat immediate score-floater speech as a separate enhancement rather than duplicating scenario scoring rules inside the UI integration.
- The scenario's imported `ReligionScreen.lua` is a same-name full replacement, so CAI's ordinary `include("ReligionScreen")` should resolve it automatically; do not copy it or add a named include that does not exist. The official screen forces `ViewMyReligion()` into read-only review, because turn-one gameplay assigns Odin pantheons to Denmark, Norway, and Sweden, Catholicism to Rome, Islam to Al-Andalus, and preset pantheons to the remaining Christian powers. CAI must return no setup state under `RULESET_SCENARIO_VIKINGS` even if generic belief counters suggest founding or adding beliefs. The founded-religion summary should use the scenario's intended maximum of two, Catholicism and Islam. Continue using the live visible belief-instance count so those two founded religions retain the official two-unlocked/two-locked presentation, while a playable Viking's own row remains a pantheon-only view.
- Scenario Setup is data-driven: only Denmark/Cnut, Norway/Harald, and Sweden/Olof are human-playable; Al-Andalus, Byzantium, and Francia occupy locked AI slots; the Standard map, six major players, eighteen scenario city-states, and 60-turn Score victory are fixed by configuration. LoadScreen consumes the shared `LOC_LOADING_INFO_VIKING_SCENARIO`. No scenario EventPopup definitions or UI replacements exist.
- The scenario deletes `UNITOPERATION_TELEPORT_TO_CITY` and `UNITOPERATION_PLANT_FOREST`; CAI's existing UnitPanel result-registration guard for scenario-pruned rows covers the known load hazard. Great People are data-driven Generals and Admirals, including the five Vinland-capable Admirals; Tech/Civic, Government, Production, Unit, City, Trade, Great People, Civilopedia, diplomacy, and end-game screens have no additional Vikings UI wrapper. Validate their scenario data through existing accessible paths instead of adding ruleset branches unless testing exposes a mismatch.
- Safe implementation order: (1) wait for the pending Poland World Rankings/Religion regressions because Vikings changes the same shared files; (2) compose the Vikings PartialScreenHooks and World Rankings wrappers; (3) add the three accessible Overall rows; (4) make Religion Screen read-only with a two-religion maximum; (5) run static ruleset/include/tag/argument and scenario-pruned-operation checks; (6) execute the in-game matrix.
- In-game matrix: Scenario Setup for all three playable leaders and the three locked AI slots; fixed map/player/turn settings and LoadScreen narration; unavailable City States and Espionage actions; World Rankings three-row Overall order and all live Score categories/totals; Odin pantheon-only views for all three Viking civilizations; Catholic and Islamic religion rows with two-of-four beliefs, no setup/add-belief controls, and `2/2` founded religions; faith-pressure changes and religion-dependent scoring; Vinland discovery with first/second/third/later Admiral awards; city/population, Great Person, trade, pillage, raiding/settling, and turn-60 Gold/Faith score updates; scenario units, buildings, governments/policies, techs/civics, Great Generals/Admirals and activation requirements, Civilopedia pages, diplomacy/war state, final Score victory and end-game controls; close/reopen focus; and ordinary-game PartialScreenHooks, World Rankings, Religion Screen, and UnitPanel regressions.
- CAI implementation 2026-07-17 selects the official Vikings PartialScreenHooks and World Rankings wrappers before expansion/base files. The accessible Espionage action reports unavailable, while City States continues through the scenario-deleted capability. World Rankings exposes the official description, religion rule, and three joined scoring explanations as three stable Overall rows and retains the generic live Score capture. Religion setup is always read-only, the founded-religion summary uses the official maximum of two, and belief totals continue following the imported scenario screen's live instances. No scenario files, modinfo registrations, or new localization tags were required.

## War Machine scenario UI replacements and composition plan

- `DLC/WarMachineScenario/WarMachineScenario.modinfo` activates for `RULESET_SCENARIO_WARMACHINE` and registers four formal replacements with no load order: `ActionPanel_WarMachineScenario.lua`, `TopPanel_WarMachineScenario.lua`, `WorldRankings_WarMachineScenario.lua`, and `ARXManager_WarMachineScenario.lua`. CAI's load-order-100 replacements therefore win the first three relevant contexts and must explicitly compose their official wrappers. ARX has no CAI accessibility context to merge. The installed and decompiled manifest and three relevant wrapper files have matching SHA-256 hashes; the manifest hash is `1338F8B1ABA806D0BDE2652C3925B15458A6A339189E030F48CDB47895D2B104`.
- Add ruleset-first branches to `ActionPanel_CAI.lua`, `TopPanel_CAI.lua`, and `WorldRankings_CAI.lua`, before the Black Death and expansion/base branches. Each official War Machine file already includes its required underlying UI (`ActionPanel_Expansion2`, `TopPanel_Expansion2`, or its own full World Rankings implementation), so CAI must not include an expansion/base file a second time. No scenario file copy or CAI modinfo registration is needed because the scenario imports all three wrappers and its World Rankings XML.
- `ActionPanel_WarMachineScenario.lua` overrides `OnRefresh()` after including Expansion 2. It deliberately calls `BASE_OnRefresh()` and hides Era/Age controls, animations, score, thresholds, and timer-warning art because the scenario deletes `CAPABILITY_ERAS`. CAI's existing `OnRefresh` wrapper can remain outside this official override and continue speaking the live end-turn tooltip. Replace the current Black-Death-only Era/Age hotkey exception with a capability check: when `CAPABILITY_ERAS` is absent, speak the existing localized unavailable message and do not inspect `Game.GetEras()`.
- `TopPanel_WarMachineScenario.lua` overrides `RefreshTurnsRemaining()` and is the authoritative source for the scenario's normalized `current/40` display and its daily calendar from August 4 through September 12, 1914. CAI's on-demand turn/time/date action already reads `Controls.Turns` and `Controls.CurrentDate`, so composing the wrapper preserves the correct values. The turn-begin announcement should call `RefreshTurnsRemaining()` and read those same live controls instead of combining raw `Game.GetCurrentGameTurn()` with a possibly stale date.
- `WorldRankings_WarMachineScenario.lua` is a full older World Rankings implementation paired with an imported XML whose Overall view contains only `WarMachine1`, `WarMachine2`, and `WarMachine3`. Its official `ViewOverall()` fills them, in order, from `LOC_WARMACHINE_SCENARIO_NAME`, `LOC_WARMACHINE_SCENARIO_ERA_INDUSTRIAL_DESCRIPTION`, and `LOC_VICTORY_WARMACHINE_SCENARIO_TT`. The first value is only the scenario title and duplicates the surrounding context, so CAI intentionally omits it. The accessible Overall view contains two stable `StaticText` rows: the scenario description followed by the France/Germany objective.
- Unlike the current base/expansion World Rankings files, the War Machine full replacement declares `TAB_SCORE`, `TAB_OVERALL`, `TAB_SCIENCE`, `TAB_CULTURE`, `TAB_RELIGION`, and `TAB_DOMINATION` as private locals. CAI cannot read those values after `include(...)`. Define CAI-owned localized tab labels with the ordinary exported globals as the first choice and the corresponding `LOC_WORLD_RANKINGS_*_TAB` lookups as fallbacks, then use those CAI labels for captured-tab mapping, rebuild dispatch, and view synchronization. This preserves ordinary wrappers and prevents nil tab mappings under War Machine.
- Only `VICTORY_SCORE` remains enabled. The scenario renames it to War Machine Victory and makes `CATEGORY_SCENARIO1` / `LINE_ITEM_CONTROL_OF_PARIS` the only scoring category with a nonzero multiplier. The gameplay script initializes France's `ScoringScenario1` value to `1`; Germany's capture of Paris ends the game through the victory requirement rather than a UI-side score calculation. CAI's existing official Score population capture should expose the live player/team ordering, score, and Control of Paris detail without a War Machine-specific score implementation.
- `EndGameMenu_WarMachineScenario.lua` is an addition loaded automatically by base `include("EndGameMenu_", true)`, the same wildcard host that imports `EndGameMenu_CAI.lua`. It changes the Score victory style to the War Machine movie and time ribbon. Scenario data disables One More Turn for every victory/defeat, gives France victory at the turn limit, gives Germany victory on capturing the Paris plot, and gives Germany a time defeat when the limit expires. Preserve the wildcard composition; do not copy or directly include the addition. Although five historic-ranking localization pairs ship, the scenario deletes every `HistoricRankings` database row and adds none, so CAI should correctly omit the Ranking tab rather than exposing those unused strings.
- War Machine is multiplayer-only (`SupportsSinglePlayer=0`), so exclusion from the single-player Scenario Setup list is correct. Its accessible launch path is the ordinary Host Game flow, including Hotseat: fixed 40 turns, fixed WWI Western Front map, France and Germany in the two selectable participant slots, and Britain and Belgium in locked slots. The existing data-driven HostGame and StagingRoom accessibility should expose ruleset choice, leaders, player state, validation, and launch without a scenario-specific frontend branch.
- Remaining content is data-driven. The ruleset removes culture/civics, governments, religion, trade, espionage, governors, Great Works, climate, World Congress, most lenses, and many ordinary units/buildings, while retaining six scenario technologies, a compact military roster, railroad-building Military Engineers, four generic Great Generals, permanent alliances and wars, and Luxembourg as a Trade city-state with France initialized as suzerain. Existing capability checks and live Tech Tree, Production, Unit, City, Great People, City States, Civilopedia, diplomacy-status, combat, and cursor paths should consume this data. The existing UnitPanel hash guard is required because the scenario prunes operations/commands such as `UNITOPERATION_PLANT_FOREST`, `UNITOPERATION_CLEAR_CONTAMINATION`, and `UNITCOMMAND_ACTIVATE_GREAT_PERSON` before re-adding only the supported command types.
- Safe implementation order: (1) add the ruleset-first Action Panel, Top Panel, and World Rankings includes; (2) generalize Era/Age unavailability to `CAPABILITY_ERAS`; (3) make turn-begin speech refresh and read the official Top Panel controls; (4) add the two-row accessible Overall branch; (5) statically verify include order, imported-file availability, localization order, wildcard End Game composition, capability gating, and absence of CAI modinfo changes; (6) run the planned in-game matrix.
- In-game matrix: create/launch Internet or Hotseat games; verify France/Germany choice and locked Britain/Belgium slots; LoadScreen player/civilization details; correct turn `1/40` through `40/40` and August/September dates on demand and at turn start; end-turn blocker speech with no Era/Age data; two World Rankings Overall rows with no redundant title; Score with live Control of Paris data and multiplayer filtering; France's turn-limit victory, Germany's Paris-capture victory, Germany's time defeat, War Machine end-game styling, no One More Turn, and no Ranking tab; six-tech tree including repeatable Industrial Warfare; military production, formations, Great General aura, engineers/railroads/forts/airstrips, aircraft, combat modifiers, city capture, Luxembourg/suzerainty, Civilopedia, and all capability-disabled actions; close/reopen and hotseat player handoff; ordinary Expansion 2 Action Panel, Top Panel, World Rankings, and End Game regressions.
- CAI implementation 2026-07-17 selects the official War Machine ActionPanel, TopPanel, and WorldRankings files before other scenario/expansion/base files. Era/Age reads follow `CAPABILITY_ERAS`; turn-start speech refreshes and reads the official turn/date controls; World Rankings uses CAI-owned tab-label fallbacks and exposes the description and objective as two Overall rows while omitting the redundant scenario-title row and retaining captured live Score data. EndGame remains automatic through its wildcard host. No scenario files, modinfo entries, or new localization tags were added.

## Tech and civic boost popup

- The boost event's `iTechProgress` / `iCivicProgress` value is the progress before the boost. After a completion boost, `PlayerTechs:GetResearchProgress(index)` or `PlayerCulture:GetCulturalProgress(index)` can already return `0` because the completed item is no longer progressing. Use `PlayerTechs:HasTech(index)` / `PlayerCulture:HasCivic(index)` as the authoritative completion state; completed boosts end at 100% and use the vanilla localized completion description.

## Research and civic chooser relationships

- Chooser rows can derive their outgoing tree relationships by reversing `GameInfo.TechnologyPrereqs()` (`PrereqTech` -> `Technology`) or `GameInfo.CivicPrereqs()` (`PrereqCivic` -> `Civic`). Use the local player's `IsTechRevealed(index)` / `IsCivicRevealed(index)` result before speaking each destination name; unrevealed destinations use the same localized `Not revealed` label as their corresponding tree.

## Great Works Overview and Showcase parity audit

- The installed and decompiled base `GreatWorksOverview.lua` / `GreatWorkShowcase.lua`, Expansion 2 overview override, Babylon Heroes overview/showcase additions, and Kublai Khan/Vietnam Monopolies overview/showcase additions have matching SHA-256 hashes. These are the complete official Great Works UI variants in the installed game. Indonesia/Khmer's manifest-only `UI/GreatWorksOverview.lua` remains absent from both copies and is not an additional implementation.
- Both base screens are wildcard hosts. CAI's files are imported at load order 50 after the official additions and wrap the resulting globals, so Expansion 2 auto-theming, Heroes slot/tooltips/showcase handling, and Monopolies Product icons/tooltips/showcase handling remain loaded. The CAI picker uses vanilla `CanMoveWorkAtAll` and `CanMoveGreatWork`, preserving art lock turns, the full-artifact-museum rule, slot compatibility, and two-way swap compatibility.
- Accessible Product rows use the active Monopolies `GetGreatWorkTooltip` override and resolve their label's live corporation name from the Product resource. This preserves the corporation, Product yields/tourism, creation data, and `ResourceIndustries.ResourceEffectTExt` benefit. Showcase continues reading the final vanilla controls, preserving both Product corporation names and Heroes creator overrides.
- `GetValidSlotIndices()` applies Expansion 2's `GetGreatWorkSlotType(...) >= 0` rule and requires a live `GreatWorkSlotTypes` row. Both hierarchy modes and the move picker consume that filtered list, so ruleset-pruned or mod-invalid slots are skipped consistently.
- Vanilla `MoveGreatWork` keeps destination city/building in private locals for its themed-building completion/progress sounds. CAI records the pending source/destination ids around its operation request and temporarily wraps the exported destination getters only while the matching `GreatWorkMoved` refresh runs. This restores the official sound path without copying or mutating vanilla's private drag instances.
- Gallery Previous/Next moves focus to the details widget after vanilla updates the controls. The newly selected work is therefore spoken and becomes the navigation position regardless of whether cycling came from a button, Left/Right, or Alt+Left/Alt+Right.
- CAI's aggregate yield summary uses the same localized-name sort as vanilla, including Tourism in the ordered set.
- The `Open()` wrapper verifies both a local player and the visible vanilla context after calling the original, so a rejected direct/debug open cannot push an empty CAI panel.
- `GreatWorksGroupByBuildings` is a non-database CAI config value stored directly under section `UI`, with string default `"true"`, following the established internal-setting pattern in `CAI_logging.lua`. The screen keeps a live boolean initialized from `CAI.GetConfigValue("UI", "GreatWorksGroupByBuildings", "true")` and writes changes through `CAI.SetConfigValue`; it does not pass the key through metadata-driven `CAISettings`, `CAI_Settings`, `settings_CAI.sql`, or the global settings screen. Its screen-local checkbox is the Great Works panel's last child. Checked builds `building -> city -> slot` in the overview and `building -> city -> work` in the move/swap picker; unchecked builds `city -> building -> slot/work`. Slot/work focus keys and all move/view eligibility are shared by both hierarchies.
- In building-first mode, the outer building already supplies the building name. City-node tooltips therefore omit that repeated name while retaining per-city theming status and providing yields/tourism.
- Great Works resolves each slot-owning building instance to its plot by scanning the owning city's `Map.GetCityPlots():GetPurchasedPlots(city)` results and matching `CityBuildings:GetBuildingsAtLocation(plotIndex)`, the same authoritative path used by Reports. In city-first mode the slot-owning building row appends its live navigation-cursor-relative direction; in building-first mode the slot-owning city row does so because it represents that building instance. Enter on either row sends `LuaEvents.CAICursorMoveTo(plotIndex, "jump")` without closing the screen; the attached `activate` listener intentionally makes Enter an action while Left/Right retain tree expansion and collapse.
## Climate Screen vanilla parity audit

- The installed Gathering Storm `ClimateScreen.lua` / XML and Gran Colombia & Maya `ClimateScreen_GranColombia_Maya.lua` / XML exactly match the copies under `decompiled/`; no other official Climate Screen Lua variants are installed.
- Vanilla Event History gates a non-global event on revelation of `kEvent.CurrentLocation`, but displays the location from `kEvent.StartLocation`. CAI uses that same split: `CurrentLocation` decides visibility, while the spoken historical location and cursor jump use `StartLocation`.
- When the current random event is a `SEA_LEVEL` event, vanilla hides the ordinary current-event card and shows separate `New` indicators on Polar Ice and Sea Level. CAI carries the two official recent-update tooltip strings into the corresponding accessible rows.
- Vanilla current-event affected-city entries pair each city name with a civilization icon whose tooltip contains the owning civilization. CAI speaks each visible affected city as city plus owning civilization.
- Vanilla's CO2-by-civilization rows use `CivilizationIcon:SetLeaderTooltip(playerID)`. CAI speaks leader plus civilization for the local contribution and every met contributor, while retaining unmet-player masking. The numeric footprint, local-player contribution, per-resource contributions, and global resource totals match vanilla.
- A revealed, non-global current event exposes `CurrentLocation`; its accessible row appends the live navigation-cursor-relative direction and is an actionable `TreeItem`. A visible non-climate Event History row exposes `StartLocation`; its row appends the same live direction and is a `Button`. Enter sends `LuaEvents.CAICursorMoveTo(plotIndex, "jump")` without closing the Climate Screen. Global live events, unrevealed live events, and locationless climate-phase history rows remain non-actionable and do not expose a cursor direction.
- Although the Gran Colombia & Maya manifest formally replaces Climate Screen for Expansion 2, CAI must include `ClimateScreen_GranColombia_Maya` only when `GAMEMODE_APOCALYPSE` is active. Firaxis does not make its forest-fire localization tags available to the in-game locale database outside the mode; composing the wrapper there makes its controls and speech expose raw `LOC_CLIMATE_FOREST_FIRE*` tags. This conditional is intentional and must not be generalized to DLC ownership or ruleset alone. CAI's accessible forest-fire row remains additionally gated on both `GameClimate.GetFirePercentChance` and `RANDOM_EVENT_FOREST_FIRE_TRIGGERED`, while its comet-strike damage interpretation is reconstructed directly.
- CAI exposes all textual/numeric vanilla content: current weather identity/location/direction/effects/losses, climate phase and all seven phase tooltips, CO2 and temperature factors, world settings, all available forecast categories including mode-gated forest fire, polar ice, sea-level totals and forecasts, both CO2 breakdowns and last-turn consumption tooltips, and reverse-chronological event history. Vanilla's pie charts, colors, icons, phase-meter fill, wave position, and event art are visual encodings of data CAI already provides textually rather than additional numeric data.
